# üß† SHARED COOPERATIVE OPERATING ATTRIBUTES

These characteristics apply **across all coop models** in your system:

---

## üîπ Governance & Decision Rights

**Member classes (A‚ÄìG)** define rights, for example:

| Class | Voting Rights            | Economic Rights        | Decision Role     |
| ----- | ------------------------ | ---------------------- | ----------------- |
| A     | Yes                      | Wages + Patronage      | Operational voice |
| B     | Advisory / some votes    | Strategic allocations  | Steward input     |
| C     | Board governance         | Oversight              | Strategic policy  |
| D     | Council advisory         | Shared commons benefit | Council influence |
| E     | Founder guidance         | Structured allocation  | Vision alignment  |
| F     | No standard vote         | Economic participation | Capital decisions |
| G     | Limited (future members) | Developmental          | Talent pipeline   |

Decision archetypes:

üîπ **Strategic:** Board + member vote
üîπ **Operational:** Management + councils
üîπ **Mission/Program:** Councils + domain experts
üîπ **Finance/Capital:** Capital coop board + investor terms

---

## üîπ Revenue & Surplus Flow

A simplified flow:

```
 OPERATIONS
 (Sales/Fees/Contracts)
       ‚Üì
 EXPENSES
       ‚Üì
 SURPLUS
       ‚Üì
 PATRONAGE ALLOCATIONS
       ‚Üì
 MEMBER DISTRIBUTIONS
```

**Key dynamics:**
‚úî Surplus distributed primarily via patronage (non-taxable at entity level)
‚úî Bylaws define surplus allocation rules
‚úî Debt service and capital reserves are paid *before patronage*

---

## üîπ Capital Formation & Growth

Each coop can source capital using:

* Member buy-in
* Deposits/retained surplus
* External non-voting/preferred equity
* Debt, subject to board approval
* Hybrid capital through capital coops

Capital decisions must *never transfer voting control away from member governance*.

---

## üîπ Debt & Financial Obligations

Debt is *held by the coop entity*:

‚úî Board authorized borrowing within limits
‚úî Debt serviced before patronage
‚úî Members liable only to extent specified in entity docs
‚úî Debt capacity determined by coop risk policies

Common debt types:

* Bank loans
* Peer-to-coop member loans
* Bonds issued by coop
* Finance leases

---

## üîπ Continuity & Failure Modes

Operating models include provisions for:

üìå Continuity planning
üìå Backstop governance if board deadlocks
üìå Merger/affiliate integration
üìå Voluntary dissolution
üìå Historical patronage protection

Each coop model includes **continuity criteria in bylaws**.

Below is a **Capital Coop / Investor Terms suite** you can *adapt directly* into your Ashe-Pamoja governance and financial documents. It is drawn from cooperative finance practices (especially emerging cooperative capital models that allow external investment without diluting member democratic control) and real investor-friendly instruments used by cooperative lenders and capital providers. ([Coop Exchange][1])

---

# üß± CAPITAL COOP / INVESTOR TERMS TEMPLATE

*(for use in bylaws, operating agreements, or investment term sheets)*

---

## 1) OVERVIEW

**Purpose:**
To enable your cooperative to raise capital from member and external investors *without compromising cooperative democratic control*, as permitted by cooperative principles and supported by modern cooperative capital practices. ([Coop Exchange][2])

Capital may be raised in any of the following forms:

‚úî **Investor Shares** (restricted / non-voting)
‚úî **Preferred Shares** (limited dividend rights)
‚úî **Investment Notes / Bonds** (debt instruments)
‚úî **Crowdfunded Equity Instruments**
‚úî **Hybrid Instruments** (e.g., convertible notes with conditions)

These terms must be incorporated into your **Capital Coop governance documents** (bylaws or standalone investment agreement).

---

## 2) DEFINITIONS (TERMINOLOGY)

**Member Equity Shares:** Equity purchased by members upon joining, granting governance rights per ‚Äúone member, one vote.‚Äù
**Investor Shares:** Shares issued to external or internal investors with *limited or no voting rights*. ([Coop Exchange][3])
**Preferred Shares:** Non-voting equity with a *fixed dividend right*, subject to board declaration and coop financial performance. ([Cooperatives][4])
**Investment Notes:** Debt instruments issued by the coop with a *defined term and interest rate*, subordinate to senior coop debt. ([Shared Capital Cooperative][5])
**Hybrid Instruments:** Custom capital instruments combining features of equity and debt, typically convertible under cooperative governance terms.

---

## 3) ISSUING INVESTOR & PREFERRED SHARES

### A. **Right to Issue**

The Capital Coop may issue one or more classes of Investor and/or Preferred Shares to raise capital, subject to governance approval and regulatory compliance.

### B. **Voting Rights**

* **Investor Shares** shall carry **no general voting rights**.
* **Preferred Shares** shall be **non-voting except in limited situations** (e.g., failure to make dividend payments).
  Members retain all governance control (board elections, bylaws, strategic decisions). ([Coop Exchange][3])

### C. **Dividend / Return Terms**

* Dividends on preferred or investor shares are **at the discretion of the Board**, subject to financial ability.
* Dividend rates may be **fixed or a range** (example: 3‚Äì8% range, as seen in practice). ([Shared Capital Cooperative][5])
* Dividends are **not cumulative** unless expressly provided.

### D. **Redemption & Liquidity**

* Shares are **not tradable on public markets by default**.
* Redemption may occur at coop discretion ‚Äî *not a demand right* ‚Äî to preserve financial stability.
* If tradable equity models are adopted in the future it must be through *restricted cooperative platforms* that preserve member control. ([Coop Exchange][6])

### E. **Capital Use & Priority**

* Preferred dividends must be paid before member patronage dividends in any given fiscal year if they are declared. ([Shared Capital Cooperative][5])
* In dissolution or liquidation, **debt holders are paid first**, then preferred/investor shares (subject to terms), then member equity/patronage allocations.

---

## 4) INVESTMENT NOTES / BONDS (DEBT)

### A. **Issuance**

The capital coop may issue **Investment Notes** or bonds to both member and non-member investors as a form of debt capital. ([Shared Capital Cooperative][5])

### B. **Terms**

* **Term Lengths:** e.g., 3, 5, 7, or 10 years
* **Interest Rates:** Defined at issuance (e.g., 3‚Äì5% range)
* **Payment Terms:** Balloon at maturity or periodic interest payments

### C. **Subordination**

Investment Notes are **unsecured and subordinated** to senior coop debt where specified. 

### D. **Redemption**

Notes are repaid at maturity or per agreed schedule; prepayment may be allowed if terms permit.

---

## 5) EQUITY CROWDFUNDING OPTIONS

### A. **Investor Shares via Crowdfunding**

The coop may engage in **equity crowdfunding** of non-voting shares to mission-aligned investors. ([Coop Exchange][7])

### B. **Community Participation**

Crowdfunding allows broad participation without transfer of control, aligning capital raising with cooperative values and community engagement.

### C. **Documentation and Compliance**

Crowdfunding offerings must be clearly documented and compliant with applicable securities and cooperative laws.

---

## 6) GOVERNANCE SAFEGUARDS

### A. **Member Control**

Voting rights for strategic decisions must remain with members, unaffected by investor capital. Issuance of investor equity *must not dilute member governance*. ([Coop Exchange][1])

### B. **Bylaws Conditions**

Any issuance must be approved under the coop‚Äôs bylaws, including:

* Creation of share classes
* Dividend and redemption policies
* Conditions for using investor capital

### C. **Supermajority Thresholds**

* Amendments affecting member rights, share issuance limits, or governance structure may require a **supermajority member vote** (e.g., 2/3 or 3/4).

---

## 7) TAX & ACCOUNTING TREATMENT

### A. **Investor Shares**

Returns (dividends) on investor or preferred shares are typically taxable to holders; the coop records them as distributions per tax law.

### B. **Debt Instruments**

Interest paid on investment notes/bonds is usually a deductible expense for the cooperative and reportable as income by investors.

### C. **Cooperative Equity**

Member equity and restricted investor equity should be tracked separately in accounts.

---

## 8) EXAMPLE TERM STRUCTURE (FILLABLE)

| Term                       | Specification                |
| -------------------------- | ---------------------------- |
| Share Class                | ___________                  |
| Eligible Investors         | Members / Non-Members / Both |
| Voting Rights              | ___________                  |
| Dividend Rate              | ___________                  |
| Dividend Payment Frequency | ___________                  |
| Redemption Terms           | ___________                  |
| Minimum Investment         | ___________                  |
| Priority in Liquidation    | ___________                  |

---

## 9) RISK DISCLOSURES & COMPLIANCE NOTES

Investments in cooperative equity or debt carry risks, including limited liquidity and the cooperative‚Äôs performance. All offerings should include full disclosure to investors and comply with securities law as required.

External investor capital is compatible with cooperative philosophy **only when it doesn‚Äôt undermine member control or risk demutualization**. ([Coop Exchange][2])

---

# üìå KEY TAKEAWAYS FOR YOUR ECOSYSTEM

‚úÖ Capital can be raised without sacrificing governance. ([Coop Exchange][1])
‚úÖ Classes of non-voting/perferred investor shares allow financial return. ([Coop Exchange][3])
‚úÖ Investment notes/bonds bring debt capital while protecting control. ([Shared Capital Cooperative][5])
‚úÖ Equity crowdfunding is another tool for aligned investors. ([Coop Exchange][7])
‚úÖ Member supermajority votes and bylaws protect democratic structure.

---

Here‚Äôs how **cooperative funds, fund structures (like GP/LP), PPMs, accounting, and financial operations** work in a mixed cooperative + investment context ‚Äî adapted for your Ashe/Pamoja ecosystem ‚Äî including how they **interface with private-equity style structures** while preserving cooperative identity and democratic control.

---

# üß† 1) FUND STRUCTURES IN GENERAL (GP/LP, LPA, PPM) ‚Äî TRADITIONAL MODEL

Before adapting to coops, here‚Äôs how typical investment funds work:

### üîπ **GP/LP Fund Structure (Private Equity / VC)**

* **General Partner (GP)** ‚Äî runs the fund, makes investments, takes management fees and carried interest.
* **Limited Partners (LPs)** ‚Äî passive capital providers with limited liability; they receive returns based on the fund agreement.
* The **Limited Partnership Agreement (LPA)** governs terms, rights, compensation, distribution waterfall, capital calls, etc. ([Wikipedia][1])

Typical terms include:

* **Management fees** (e.g., 1‚Äì2%)
* **Carried interest** (GP share of profits above hurdle)
* **Distribution waterfall** allocating returns first to return capital, then preferred return, then carry to GP. ([Wikipedia][2])

### üîπ **Private Placement Memorandum (PPM)**

* A document used to offer investment interests in a fund.
* Discloses risks, strategy, terms, projected returns, fees, governance, redemption and transfer restrictions.
* Used to comply with securities laws when offering LP interests.

### Audits & Reporting

* Investors typically get quarterly reporting, audits, capital call notices, distribution notices, etc.
* Fund administration ensures compliance with tax and securities law.

---

# üß† 2) HOW THESE TRADITIONAL FUNDS MAP TO *COOPERATIVE* REALITY

**Pure cooperatives cannot simply adopt a GP/LP model as-is** because:

‚úî Coops emphasize **democratic member control** (one member, one vote) not capital control. ([Wikipedia][3])
‚úî Members are collectively sovereign, not residual claimants like corporate shareholders.
‚úî Standard LP economic rights tied to control are incompatible with coop governance.

But you *can* use **investment fund structures that are compatible with coop values** by combining cooperative entities with structured investment vehicles (SPVs, LLCs, or hybrid funds) that partner with a coop.

---

# üß† 3) COOPERATIVE FUNDS FOR YOUR ECOSYSTEM

### A) **Coop Capital Fund (Internal Coop Investment Pool)**

**Purpose:**

* Pool capital from coops and members to invest in coop ventures.

**Structure:**

* The fund itself is a **cooperative** or **multi-stakeholder coop** (members include coops and capital participants).
* No GP/LP with control rights ‚Äî governance is democratic.

**Financing:**

* Member equity contributions
* Possibly issuance of **non-voting investor shares** or debt instruments (bonds) where allowed under coop bylaws to attract external capital without diluting control. ([Coop Exchange][4])

**Operating Principles:**

* Investment decisions recommended by an Investment Committee, approved by member vote or board
* Profits returned via predetermined cooperative distribution rules (not carried interest)
* Financial rights may be defined in bylaws or investment policy

**Notes:**

* A cooperative fund in this model doesn‚Äôt operate as a blind GP/LP private equity fund; income allocation is based on coop principles and patronage rules.

---

### B) **Hybrid Fund Vehicles (SPVs or LLCs)**

To combine **cooperative capital with structured external investment**, you might create a *parallel investment entity*:

**Example Structure:**

```
          Pamoja Unified Coop Fund (Cooperative)
                       |
             LLC/LP Fund Vehicle (SPV)
             /                     \
      External Investors        Cooperative Capital
```

**How it works:**

* The **coop** remains the governor of mission and member oversight.
* A **fund vehicle (LLC or limited partnership)** receives external capital under an LPA or investment agreement.
* Distribution rights and economics are clearly spelled out in the LPA/PPM.
* The coop can be the **investment advisor or co-investor** and often holds a strategic stake but **does not cede governance** of the coop.

**Why this model is useful:**

* Provides a legally familiar structure to **institutional investors** (LPs). ([Foley & Lardner LLP][5])
* Preserves coop governance in core operational entities while facilitating external capital participation.
* Can employ **capital calls** and structured returns common in private investment funds. ([Alter Domus][6])

This is **not a coop itself**, but a *fund architecture compatible* with coops and investor frameworks.

---

### C) **Cooperative Investment Pool (No GP/LP)**

For a completely cooperative approach, establish a **pooled investment coop** where:

* Each member (coop or individual) contributes capital.
* Governance operates democratically.
* Returns are distributed by cooperative bylaws (often as patronage or limited dividends under coop principles). ([Coop Exchange][4])
* No single GP entity manages ‚Äî instead, an elected committee or board oversees capital allocation.

This model favors democratic control but may be less attractive to traditional LP investors without structured returns.

---

# üß† 4) PRIVATE PLACEMENT MEMORANDUM (PPM) ADAPTED

If you raise capital (especially externally) you should use a **PPM or fundraising disclosure** even in cooperative contexts:

**Content of a Coop Fund PPM may include:**
‚úî Purpose and mission
‚úî Governance and voting rights
‚úî Type of capital accepted (non-voting investor shares, debt)
‚úî Risk factors
‚úî Distribution policy (how returns are allocated)
‚úî Liquidity / redemption restrictions
‚úî Tax treatment for investors

This protects transparency and compliance with securities regulations, especially if issuing interests to accredited or non-member investors.

---

# üß† 5) FINANCIAL & ACCOUNTING SYSTEMS FOR COOPS AND FUNDS

### A) **Cooperative Financial Accounting**

Coops use standard business accounting systems, but with specific adaptations:

**Equity Accounts**

* Maintain separate member equity accounts
* Track patronage allocations separately from retained earnings

**Surplus Treatment**

* Surpluses may be allocated to members as **patronage refunds** instead of corporate profit distributions.
* Patronage accounting follows specific tax rules if deducted at the entity level.

**Debt vs Capital**

* Debt is recorded as liability; member or external capital as equity
* Preferred or investor equity is tracked distinctly

**Budgeting & Reporting**

* Annual budgets approved by board or members
* Monthly or quarterly financial reporting
* Audit or review based on size/requirements

### B) **Funds & Investment Accounting**

If a fund vehicle exists (LLC/LPA style):

* **Capital commitments** and **capital calls** recorded
* **Investor contributions** tracked with membership interests
* Distribution waterfall *if used* outlined in LPA
* Regular investor reporting (IRR, cash flows, valuations) is standard

While cooperatives themselves won‚Äôt use traditional private equity waterfall *inside the coop*, a **fund vehicle** has its own accounting for investor economics. ([Wikipedia][2])

---

# üß† 6) NOTES ON TAX & REGULATORY COMPLIANCE

**Cooperative Funds (Internal)**

* Follow cooperative tax principles (patronage allocations, bylaws compliance)
* Member distributions reported per tax classification

**Hybrid Fund Vehicles**

* If structured as LLC/LP, taxable income passes through partners (no entity tax) and each investor reports their share; or depending on structure may elect corporate tax
* Securities laws may apply if offering interests externally ‚Äî so PPM and compliance is critical.

**External Investment Compliance**

* State and federal securities law must be observed
* Disclosure requirements apply if investors are not all members

---

# üß† 7) PRACTICAL ARCHITECTURE FOR YOUR ECOSYSTEM

You can layer these as follows:

```
                        Pamoja Coop Capital Pool
                       (Democratic Cooperative)
                                   |
         ----------------------------------------------------
         |                                                  |
Internal Impact Fund                              External Capital Fund Vehicle
(Cooperative, member capital)            (LLC/LP with LPA/PPM for investors)
         |                                                  |
 Ventures & Projects                               Targeted Investments
```

**How it works:**

* All coop members may vote on investment policy in the cooperative capital pool.
* For large external capital, a **parallel fund vehicle** is created with clear investor terms (LPA + PPM).
* The cooperative provides advisory/manager services to the fund but remains mission steward.

---

# üìå SUMMARY KEY POINTS

| Feature          | Pure Coop Fund                             | Hybrid Fund Vehicle                |
| ---------------- | ------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------- |
| Governance       | Democratic member control                  | Manager/GP + LP investors          |
| Legal Form       | Cooperative                                | LLC/LP (LPA)                       |
| Capital Sources  | Members, non-voting investor shares, bonds | Accredited investors, institutions |
| Compliance Doc   | Bylaws, investment policy                  | LPA + PPM                          |
| Return Structure | Cooperative distributions                  | Waterfalls, preferred returns      |
| Tax              | Patronage, cooperative tax rules           | Flow-through (LLC/LPA) tax rules   |

---

Below is a **sample outline ‚Äî tailored** for a **hybrid cooperative investment vehicle‚Äôs Private Placement Memorandum (PPM)** that you can use as a blueprint for capital raises while preserving cooperative governance. It‚Äôs based on widely used sections in PPMs and adapted to include cooperative-specific governance and investor terms. ([Private Placement Memorandum][1])

> ‚ö†Ô∏è *Note:* A PPM is a legal document designed to comply with securities regulations if you‚Äôre offering interests to external investors. Many jurisdictions exempt small, family-member only investments, but if external (even non-voting) investor capital is involved you‚Äôll want disclosures. ([JD Supra][2])

---

# üìÑ **SAMPLE PPM OUTLINE ‚Äî HYBRID COOP INVESTMENT VEHICLE**

---

## **I. COVER PAGE**

‚úî Name of the Cooperative Fund
‚úî Type of Offering (e.g., non-voting investor shares / debt instruments)
‚úî Address and contact info
‚úî Date of PPM
‚úî Confidentiality notice

---

## **II. TABLE OF CONTENTS**

Organize so readers can easily jump to key sections.

---

## **III. IMPORTANT NOTICES & LEGENDS**

‚úî Federal and state securities law legends
‚úî Statements on exempt offering status
‚úî No public market for securities offered

> Must include legal disclaimers and jurisdictional compliance notes. ([Private Placement Memorandum][1])

---

## **IV. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY**

‚úî Summary of the investment vehicle purpose
‚úî Total capital targeted
‚úî Type of instruments offered (non-voting shares, preferred shares, notes, etc.)
‚úî High-level terms (pricing, minimum subscription, expected timeline)

---

## **V. INVESTMENT OPPORTUNITY

A. Description of the Cooperative Capital Vehicle
‚úî Mission + cooperative governance model
‚úî How it aligns with cooperative principles
‚úî Relationship between coop members and external investors

B. Market Context & Strategy (for fund deployment)

C. Competitive & Differentiated Position

---

## **VI. TERMS OF THE OFFERING**

‚úî Type and class of interest being offered
‚úî Price per unit of security
‚úî Minimum investment amount
‚úî Rights of investors (economic rights only; no governance rights)
‚úî Expected term of investment or maturity dates (if debt)
‚úî Dividend / interest / return provisions

---

## **VII. CAPITALIZATION & OWNERSHIP STRUCTURE**

‚úî Pre-offer and post-offer capital structure
‚úî Member vs investor instrument breakdown
‚úî Impact on cooperative governance

---

## **VIII. USE OF PROCEEDS**

‚úî How funds will be used
(e.g., investment into ventures, reserves, working capital, debt repayment)

---

## **IX. RISK FACTORS**

A front-loaded and detailed section with risks such as:

‚úî Investment not assured of return
‚úî Illiquidity of instruments
‚úî Operational risks of ventures funded
‚úî Risks unique to cooperative structures
‚úî Regulatory risks

> PPMs spend substantial effort on tailored risk disclosures. ([Capital Fund Law Group][3])

---

## **X. MANAGEMENT & GOVERNANCE**

‚úî Bios of founders / managers
‚úî Track record
‚úî Roles of cooperative governance vs investor expectations
‚úî Boards, committees, and decision processes

---

## **XI. DISCLAIMER & LEGAL INFORMATION**

‚úî Securities offered only under exempt status
‚úî Restrictions on transfer / resale
‚úî No public trading market

---

## **XII. TAX CONSIDERATIONS**

‚úî How distributions / returns are treated for tax purposes
‚úî Cooperative patronage / withholding rules
‚úî External investor tax implications

---

## **XIII. SUBSCRIPTION PROCEDURES**

‚úî How to subscribe
‚úî Required investor acknowledgements
‚úî Accredited / qualified investor standards (if applicable)

---

## **XIV. INVESTOR SUITABILITY & QUESTIONNAIRE**

‚úî Questionnaire confirming investor status & financial sophistication
‚úî Acknowledgment of risk and investment horizon

---

## **XV. SUBSCRIPTION AGREEMENT**

‚úî Contract between issuer and investor
‚úî Terms of the agreement
‚úî Representations and warranties

---

## **XVI. DESCRIPTION OF SECURITIES**

‚úî Detailed definition of the securities being issued
‚úî Rights, preferences, and limitations of each class
‚úî Redemption / redemption restrictions

---

## **XVII. FINANCIAL INFORMATION & PROJECTIONS**

‚úî Historical results (if any) of the coop/fund
‚úî Forecasts (revenue / distributions) as applicable

---

## **XVIII. MATERIAL CONTRACTS & EXHIBITS**

‚úî Key docs (bylaws, board resolution to issue securities)
‚úî Organizational docs
‚úî Relevant agreements (e.g., management, advisory)

---

## **XIX. LEGAL & REGULATORY NOTICES**

‚úî Blue sky / state law disclosures as needed
‚úî Legal compliance statements

---

## **XX. DEFINITIONS**

‚úî Clear definitions of terms used throughout the PPM

---

## **XXI. INVESTMENT CONTACT & ADMINISTRATION**

‚úî Issuer contact info
‚úî Fund administrator details

---

# üìå OPTIONAL ATTACHMENTS

üìç Business Plan (full or summarized)
üìç Operating / Partnership Agreements
üìç Audited or Compiled Financials
üìç Independent Legal Opinion Letter

---

# üìå WHY THESE SECTIONS MATTER

‚úî A PPM *provides full disclosure* so investors can make informed decisions. ([Private Placement Memorandum][1])
‚úî It also *protects the issuer* from future disputes by detailing risks, terms, and legal compliance. ([Capital Fund Law Group][3])
‚úî Sections like ‚ÄúRisk Factors‚Äù and ‚ÄúUse of Proceeds‚Äù are essential to meet investor expectations and regulatory norms. ([Private Placement Memorandum][1])

---

# üìå ADAPTATIONS FOR YOUR HYBRID COOP MODEL

Since your fund exists within a cooperative ecosystem:

### üü¢ **Emphasize governance structure**

Explain how *cooperative governance* interacts with investor economics (e.g., member voting stays intact; investors have economic rights but not control).

### üü¢ **Explain instrument limitations**

State clearly in the **Description of Securities** how non-voting shares or debt instruments differ from member equity.

### üü¢ **Tailor risk sections**

Highlight coop-specific risks (e.g., cooperative mission impacts, patronage variability, legal structure complexities).

### üü¢ **Tax treatment**

Include how distributions are taxed for investors and members differently.

Below is a **custom LPA draft outline** tailored for a *hybrid coop-aligned investment vehicle* ‚Äî one that blends **cooperative governance principles** with traditional **GP/LP fund structure mechanics**. Use this as a **structural template** for your legal drafting (and provide it to counsel for jurisdiction-specific preparation).

I‚Äôve adapted private equity LPA concepts (from industry standard templates like the ILPA Model LPA, which provides foundational structure and clauses for GP/LP funds)([ILPA][1]) while embedding **cooperative safeguards** so the coop‚Äôs democratic & mission-aligned control isn‚Äôt undermined.

---

# üìÑ HYBRID COOPERATIVE FUND LPA ‚Äî DRAFT OUTLINE

> ‚ö† **Legal draft guidance only.** This is a structural framework; you must engage counsel to turn this into a legally enforceable document.

---

## **1. TITLE & PREAMBLE**

```
LIMITED PARTNERSHIP AGREEMENT
OF
[COOPERATIVE CAPITAL FUND NAME], LIMITED PARTNERSHIP
(Dated as of [Date])
```

**Parties:**
‚Ä¢ **General Partner (GP)**: [Entity Name, typically an LLC/management coop affiliate]
‚Ä¢ **Limited Partners (LPs)**: Investors into the Fund

State of formation, type of entity, governing law.

Purpose statement: cooperative capital deployment for ventures aligned with Pamoja mission, with democratic coop governance separate from investor economic participation.

---

## **2. DEFINITIONS & INTERPRETATIONS**

Clear definitions of all capital terms, including:

* ‚ÄúAffiliate‚Äù
* ‚ÄúAdvisory Committee‚Äù
* ‚ÄúCapital Commitment‚Äù
* ‚ÄúCooperative Governance Principles‚Äù (explicit reference to cooperative bylaws)
* ‚ÄúDistribution Waterfall‚Äù
* ‚ÄúRelated Party‚Äù
* ‚ÄúQualified Resolution‚Äù
* ‚ÄúMember Voting Rights‚Äù vs ‚ÄúInvestor Economic Rights‚Äù

*Note:* In a hybrid structure, clarify that **investor interests do not carry governance rights** in underlying coops, and only fund decisions per this LPA. Provide glossary.

---

## **3. FORMATION & PURPOSE**

* Formation of LP under [State] law
* Purpose: To pool investor capital and cooperative capital to make mission-aligned investments
* Investment policy aligned with cooperative mission (require board / member council affirmation for major strategic deviations)

This reconciles **GP/LP investment structure** with the coop‚Äôs governing principles.

---

## **4. CAPITAL CONTRIBUTIONS**

**LP Contributions**

* Initial commitments and capital call procedures
* Minimum and maximum subscription

**Coop Side**

* The cooperative entity‚Äôs contributions and nature of its role (e.g., adviser, strategic partner)

**Restrictions**

* No investor contribution gives governance control in Pamoja coops; economic rights only
* Transfer restrictions on LP interests with right of first refusal

Include provisions similar to standard LPAs for capital commitments, but **explicitly distinguish governance rights** (reserved for coop members under coop bylaws).

---

## **5. ALLOCATIONS & DISTRIBUTIONS**

**Profit Allocation Waterfall (Adapted)**

1. Return of LP capital
2. Preferred return (if applicable)
3. Surplus sharing among LPs and coop (GP) per agreed percentages

You may reference waterfall structures like the ‚Äúwhole-of-fund‚Äù model used in best-practice LPAs. ([ILPA][1])

**Cooperative Allocation**

* If coop units participate economically, allocate in line with coop policies where allowable (patronage allocations, capped preferred returns, etc.).
* Protect cooperative mission funds before economic distributions.

---

## **6. GOVERNANCE & CONTROL**

### **General Partner Authority**

‚Ä¢ Makes investment decisions
‚Ä¢ Implements strategy

### **Cooperative Advisory Committee**

‚Ä¢ Standing committee empowered to ensure investment policy aligns with coop mission
‚Ä¢ May veto or propose redirections based on cooperative bylaws

### **Limited Partner Advisory Committee (LPAC)**

‚Ä¢ Standard in LPAs to represent LP interests
‚Ä¢ Can review conflicts, approve certain actions (extensions, key person changes)

### **Coop Governance Integration**

Include language that **cooperative governance decisions (such as allocation of patronage, mission pivot, use of core IP) remain under coop governance**, and LPA fiduciary duties do not override coop bylaws.
This protects democratic member rights while allowing contractually agreed investor rights.

---

## **7. MANAGEMENT FEES & EXPENSES**

**Management Fees**

* Fee paid to GP or management affiliate (e.g., coop advisory unit)
* Clear breakdown for services, reduced or terminated post-investment period

**Expenses**

* Define which fund expenses are reimbursable

You can adapt fee terms from model LPAs (e.g., management fee reduction post investment period). ([ILPA][2])

---

## **8. STANDARD OF CARE & FIDUCIARY DUTIES**

Include dual standards:

‚úî **Standard LPA fiduciary duties** ‚Äî GP must act in good faith, prudent care to LPs. ([ILPA][2])

‚úî **Cooperative governance duties** ‚Äî follow cooperative bylaws and mission, including provision that GP actions in portfolio coops cannot violate underlying cooperatives‚Äô democratic governance.

This dual standard protects investors *and* coop values.

---

## **9. TRANSFERS & WITHDRAWALS**

**Restricted Transfers**

* LPs may not transfer interests except under approval and subject to right of first refusal

**Cooperative Constraints**

* LP interests don‚Äôt entitle governance rights in coops; transfers do not change member class rights in coop governance.

Use standard LP transfer restrictions (e.g., consent to transfer, first refusal) to protect the structure.

---

## **10. TERM, WITHDRAWAL & TERMINATION**

**Term**

* Defines investment period, term extensions per LP vote

**Withdrawal**

* LP withdrawal subject to conditions; no unilateral exit outside what‚Äôs agreed

**Dissolution**

* Upon wind-up, distributions per waterfall and cooperative transition plan

Standard practice in LPAs: capital return and liquidation provisions.

---

## **11. TAX & ALLOCATION CLAUSES**

* Solicit tax classification ‚Äî flow-through treatment
* Allocation of taxable items to LPs
* Cooperatives‚Äô tax treatment remains separate

Ensure clarity on how tax impact and reporting is handled for both investor LPs and cooperative economic participants.

---

## **12. REPORTING & INFORMATION RIGHTS**

LPs and advisory committees have:
‚úî periodic financial reporting
‚úî access to audited statements (if any)
‚úî notices of capital calls and distributions

GP must provide information in reasonable detail. This matches industry LP rights expectations in model LPAs. ([ILPA][1])

---

## **13. CONFLICTS OF INTEREST**

Define policies for related party transactions, including:

* Investments in coop-owned ventures
* Transactions among GP affiliates and coop affiliates

Advisory committee reviews conflicts before approval. Standard in model LPAs.

---

## **14. AMENDMENTS**

Changes to material economics or governance in the LPA require:
‚úî Supermajority of LPs (e.g., 2/3) **and**
‚úî Approval from a *cooperative governance body* if underlying coop structure is affected

This two-track amendment rights protects both investor and coop democratic integrity.

---

## **15. MISCELLANEOUS**

Include:

* Governing law (e.g., Delaware)
* Arbitration clauses
* Severability
* Notices

---

# üß† KEY HYBRID SAFEGUARDS BUILT IN

| Feature      | Coop-Adaptation                                                               |
| ------------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Governance   | LP interests **do not override coop member rights**                           |
| Distribution | Waterfall with investor preferred rights **but coop mission funds protected** |
| Transfers    | Restricted; cannot affect coop governance                                     |
| Conflicts    | Advisory committee oversight ensures coop principles honored                  |
| Amendments   | Dual-approval by LP supermajority **and** coop body                           |

---

# üü° WHAT THIS DRAFT TEMPLATE ACHIEVES

‚úî Uses industry LPA **structure and clauses** (e.g., waterfall, fiduciary, reporting) based on widely recognized **Model LPA frameworks**. ([ILPA][1])
‚úî Embeds **cooperative safeguards** so external capital doesn‚Äôt undermine democratic governance.
‚úî Balances **investor expectations** and **cooperative mission continuity**.
‚úî Provides a **negotiable foundation** that your attorneys and fund counsel can refine.

This shows how money and decision authority move between **Cooperative Funds, Hybrid Fund Vehicles, Operating Entities, Members, and External Investors**, while preserving cooperative principles and satisfying tax/regulatory requirements.

```
                               ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê

                               ‚îÇ (Classes A‚ÄìG)    ‚îÇ
```

---

# ‚úÖ EXPLANATIONS ‚Äî WHAT EACH COLUMN MEANS

---

## üîπ **Members (Classes A‚ÄìG)**

**Governance**

* Democratic control resides with members.
* They vote for boards, bylaws, major fund policies.
* They *do not lose voting power* even if they contribute capital.

**Tax**

* Members report patronage distributions and other income (wages, dividends) on their individual returns.

---

## üîπ **Cooperative Boards / Councils / Committees**

**Role**

* Steward investment policy for coop funds.
* Approve capital deployment and risk parameters.
* Ensure investment strategy aligns with coop mission and bylaws.

---

## üîπ **Coop Capital Pool & Internal Cooperative Fund**

**What It Is**

* A cooperative entity that pools capital from member coops and members.
* Democratically governed per coop bylaws.
* No traditional GP/LP hierarchy.

**Flows**

* Capital from members ‚Üí invested in operating coop ventures.
* Surplus from ventures ‚Üí returned as patronage or reinvested.

**Tax**

* Surplus is allocated to members as patronage.
* The coop itself generally not taxed if all surplus is patronage¬≠d (Subchapter T where applicable).

---

## üîπ **Investment Committee**

**Role**

* Appointed by cooperative board to:

  * Evaluate investment opportunities
  * Ensure mission alignment
  * Execute investment decisions within policies

**Governance Link**

* Decisions are subject to member policies via board accountability.

---

## üîπ **Operating Coop Entities (Ventures)**

**Function**

* Generate revenue and surplus through operations.

**Tax & Finance**

* These may be taxable (operating profit subject to entity tax if not fully patronaged).
* Surplus flows to capital pool and/or members via patronage or dividends as defined in bylaws.

---

## üîπ **Hybrid Fund Vehicle (LLC/LP)**

**Purpose**

* Used when external, traditional investment capital is needed.
* Provides a legal structure investors understand (LLC/LP with a PPM + LPA).

**Governance**

* Fund governance (GP/LP structure) is separate from coop governance.
* The coop funds and coop entities continue normal governance under coop bylaws.
* Investors **do not have governance control** over coop entities.

**Tax & Reporting**

* Typically pass-through tax treatment.
* LPs report their share of income/returns.
* GP entity (which can be a coop affiliate) receives management fees/carry.

---

## üîπ **Investor Rights vs. Member Governance**

Investors:

* Receive **economic rights** (preferred returns, distributions per fund documents)
* **Do NOT receive governance rights** in coop entities
* Subject to transfer restrictions & investment terms

Members:

* Retain governance rights per cooperative bylaws
* Participate in board votes, governance decisions

---

## üîπ **Tax Reporting Flows**

**Operating Surplus**

1. Operating coop surpluses go to the capital pool or retained at the coop.
2. Patronage distributions flow to members ‚Äî members pay tax individually.

**Hybrid Fund Returns**

1. LP distributions go to investors; they report income per LLC/LP terms.
2. GP/management fees reported as income by GP entity (often a coop affiliate).

**Member Equity Accounts**

* Track member capital and patronage allocations.
* Used for tax reporting and distribution history.

---

# üß† HOW THIS FITS YOUR ASHE / PAMOJA ECOSYSTEM

| Layer            | Governance        | Tax Flow                   | Capital Flow                          |
| ---------------- | ----------------- | -------------------------- | ------------------------------------- |
| Members          | Democratic        | Individual                 | Contribute capital, receive patronage |
| Cooperative Fund | Board governance  | Pass-through via patronage | Allocates to ventures                 |
| Operating Coops  | Member-controlled | Taxed as coop or entity    | Returns to capital pool               |
| Hybrid Vehicle   | GP/LP governance  | LP income tax              | External invests via PPM/LPA          |
| Investors        | Economic only     | Report investor income     | Limited rights                        |

---

# üìå HIGH-LEVEL TAKEAWAYS

‚úÖ **Governance stays with members**, not capital holders.
‚úÖ **Internal funds** operate democratically by coop bylaws.
‚úÖ **External investors** are allowed via a legal fund vehicle, *but cannot acquire governance rights in the coop*.
‚úÖ **Tax flows to the lowest accountable individual/entity**: members for patronage; investors for LP income; coop entity for retained items.
‚úÖ **Funds comply with both coop principles and investment framework expectations**.

It maps **fund structure, governance rights, tax flows, and member/investor rights** in a formally usable format so it can be appended as an annexe to your LPA/PPM or cooperative governance documents.

## Annex X ‚Äì Fund & Governance Mapping Table

| **Category**                  | **Entity/Instrument**          | **Legal Form**                         | **Governance Rights**                                                                         | **Economic Rights**                             | **Tax Treatment**                                | **Notes**                                                 |
| ----------------------------- | ------------------------------ | -------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Core Coop Entities**        | Operating Coops                | Coop Corp / LLC taxed as coop          | Member democratic control (one member, one vote)                                              | Patronage allocations, limited retained surplus | Pass-through via patronage; members report       | Must comply with state coop law; no external govt control |
|                               | Cooperative Capital Pool       | Cooperative or Multi-Stakeholder Coop  | Democratic governance by members                                                              | Profit allocation per patronage rules           | Pass-through via patronage                       | Capital use defined in bylaws                             |
|                               | Member Equity Accounts         | Internal equity                        | Voting per membership classification                                                          | Return of capital/patronage                     | Members report as income                         | Not tradable outside coop                                 |
| **Hybrid Investment Vehicle** | Fund LP / LLC Vehicle          | LLC/LP (LPA governed)                  | Governance per LPA/GP structure *does not confer governance to elect boards in coop entities* | Investor economic rights per LPA waterfall      | Flow-through (LLC/LP) taxed to LPs and GP entity | Must comply with securities law as applicable             |
|                               | GP (General Partner)           | LLC (may be coop affiliate)            | GP governance per LPA                                                                         | Management fees + carry (if provided)           | GP entity reports income                         | Confined to fund management; no coop control              |
|                               | LP (Limited Partner Interests) | LLC/LP interest                        | No governance over coop entities                                                              | Distribution of returns per LPA                 | LPs report flow-through income                   | Transfer restrictions apply                               |
| **Investment Instruments**    | Non-Voting Investor Shares     | Equity class in coop                   | No voting rights in core coop governance                                                      | Fixed dividend or share in surplus              | Dividend taxable to holder                       | Terms defined in bylaws/PPM                               |
|                               | Preferred Shares               | Equity class in coop or related entity | Limited voting (situational)                                                                  | Dividend priority                               | Dividend taxable                                 | Conditions in cooperative capital terms                   |
|                               | Debt Instruments / Bonds       | Debt contract                          | No governance rights                                                                          | Interest payments                               | Interest income taxable                          | May be tradable if supported                              |
| **Governance Bodies**         | Board of Directors (Coop)      | Elected by coop members                | Full governance; fiduciary duties to coop                                                     | N/A                                             | N/A                                              | Oversees operations & strategy                            |
|                               | Cooperative Councils           | Member representative bodies           | Advisory / delegated authority                                                                | N/A                                             | N/A                                              | Consultative authority                                    |
|                               | Investment Committee           | Appointed by Board                     | Operational investment oversight                                                              | N/A                                             | N/A                                              | Aligns with coop investment policy                        |
|                               | LP Advisory Committee          | Limited Partners                       | Advisory per LPA                                                                              | N/A                                             | N/A                                              | Reviews conflicts, major changes                          |

---

## Annex X ‚Äì Mapping Notes & Definitions

### 1. **Governance Rights**

‚ÄúGovernance Rights‚Äù reflect *control over entity direction and decisions*.

* **Member democratic control** applies in cooperatives (not based on capital invested).
* **Investor governance rights** are limited to the *fund vehicle‚Äôs internal governance*; they do **NOT include governance** of underlying coop entities unless explicitly provided in coop bylaws (which is typically prohibited to protect member control).

---

### 2. **Economic Rights Explained**

Economic rights reflect financial participation:

* **Patronage allocations** flow from coop surplus and are allocated to members based on use.
* **Investor economic rights** may include dividends, preferred payments, or LP distributions as defined in investment documents.

---

### 3. **Tax Treatment Notations**

* **Pass-through (coops)**: Cooperative surplus that is properly patronaged can often be deducted at the entity level, with members reporting as income.
* **LLC/LP flow-through**: Investors report income tax on their share of fund income; the vehicle itself typically has no entity-level tax.

---

## Annex X ‚Äì Example Cross-Reference Clauses

### A. Governing Law

> *All cooperative governance and member voting rules referenced in this Annex are subject to the cooperative statutes of [State/Country], and any inconsistencies shall be resolved in favor of statutory compliance.*

### B. No Governance by Investors in Coop Entities

> *Investor interests in the Fund or in Preferred/Investor Shares do NOT confer any governance rights in cooperative entities unless both (i) expressly permitted in the cooperative‚Äôs bylaws and (ii) approved by supermajority member vote.*

### C. Tax Reporting & Member Obligations

> *Members shall report income from patronage distributions in accordance with applicable tax law. The cooperative shall provide necessary tax reporting (Forms 1099-PATR or equivalent) in compliance with jurisdictional requirements.*

### D. Transfer Restrictions

> *Transfer of Limited Partner interests or investor shares is subject to right of first refusal, board consent, and any additional restrictions set forth in applicable governing documents.*

---

## Annex X ‚Äì Risk & Compliance Notes

1. **Securities Compliance:**
   All investor offerings (Hybrid Fund, non-voting shares, preferred shares) must include a compliant **Private Placement Memorandum (PPM)** and satisfy applicable securities exemptions or registration.

2. **Cooperative Safeguards:**
   Cooperative core governance (one member, one vote; board authority) shall not be diminished by external investment structures.

3. **Accounting Standards:**
   Financial reporting shall comply with generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP) or IFRS as applicable, with separate tracking of member equity, patronage allocations, investor economic interests, and debt.

---

* **Exhibit B:** Fund LPA (Full Text)
* **Exhibit C:** Private Placement Memorandum (PPM)
* **Exhibit D:** Investor Rights Agreements
* **Exhibit E:** Patronage Allocation Policy

Below is a **comprehensive legal entity management framework** for *all your coops and related entities* ‚Äî designed to align with your Ashe/Msingi/Pamoja ecosystem, member classes, governance structures, and financial/legal roles. This covers **legal entity design, governance, compliance, roles, relationships, and practical administration**.

I‚Äôve structured it so you can **use it directly in your legal manuals, operating agreements, and entity governance docs**.

---

# üß± 0) HIGH-LEVEL ENTITY MANAGEMENT PRINCIPLES

Before diving into specifics, your system needs a **consistent set of legal management foundations**:

### PRINCIPLE A ‚Äî *Entity Purpose First*

Each legal entity exists to fulfill a **distinct operational, governance, or capital role**.

### PRINCIPLE B ‚Äî *Governance Must Reflect Mission*

Decision rights are aligned with member class roles and democratic processes.

### PRINCIPLE C ‚Äî *Hierarchy of Authority*

Governance ‚Üí Boards ‚Üí Councils ‚Üí Committees ‚Üí Management.

### PRINCIPLE D ‚Äî *Legal Separation*

Entities must be legally separate to protect liability, control, and tax boundaries.

### PRINCIPLE E ‚Äî *Compliance & Reporting*

Every entity must adhere to statutory requirements (state corp law, IRS, securities, labor, tax, etc.).

---

# üß† 1) ENTITY TYPOLOGY & LEGAL STRUCTURES

Your ecosystem comprises **three major entity families**:

A) **Cooperatives (primary operating & governance)**
B) **Program / Nonprofit units**
C) **Capital / Hybrid vehicles and Funds**
D) **Support / Federation coops**
E) **Estates & Personal Offices**

Each has its own legal management approach.

---

# üß± 2) COOPERATIVE ENTITY MANAGEMENT

### COVERAGE

Applies to:

* All *operating business coops* (e.g., Nandi Mobility Coop, Wolof.io Coop, etc.)
* *Ubuntuwa Commons + sub-commons*
* *Specialized coops* (Moyo Collective, Bahari Network, Ubunye Engineering, Umoya Society, Kumba Metafactory)

---

## 2A ‚Äî LEGAL FORM & REGISTRATION

Each coop should be:

**Primary Form:**
‚û°Ô∏è **State Cooperative Corporation** or **LLC electing coop tax treatment**

**Registration Checklist**

* Name reservation
* Articles of Incorporation/Organization
* Registered Agent
* Member class definitions embedded
* Purpose statement aligned with coop mission
* Initial director/member appointment

*Tip:* Include a **mission lock clause** in articles to prevent sale of mission without member supermajority.

---

## 2B ‚Äî GOVERNANCE STRUCTURE

Each coop must adopt **Bylaws** that define:

### I. Member Classes (A‚ÄìG)

Each class must have:
‚úî Right to participate
‚úî Defined rights/obligations
‚úî Eligibility criteria

1. *Governance always aligns with member role, not capital alone.*
2. *Separate legal entities protect liability and mission boundaries.*
3. *Capital participation does not imply governance control.*
4. *Bylaws are binding and require supermajorities for existential changes.*
5. *Inter-entity agreements enforce lawful cooperation.*
6. *Compliance and reporting must be documented and audited.*

This was a good catch ‚Äî your ecosystem is *internally consistent*, but now you‚Äôre seeing where the legal/tax precision needs to be tightened.

Your instinct is **sound**, and it *fits your ecosystem* ‚Äî but it needs to be **structured precisely** so it does **not create tax landmines, governance confusion, or accidental equity control**.

Below is a **clean, IRS-defensible, coop-compatible model** for **sweat equity ‚Üí deferred compensation ‚Üí paid fees**, tailored to your **personal office firm + Pamoja federation**.

---

# üß≠ THE CORRECT WAY TO DO SWEAT EQUITY IN YOUR SYSTEM

## ‚ö†Ô∏è First: What ‚ÄúSweat Equity‚Äù *Cannot* Be (Legally)

For your setup, sweat equity **cannot** be:

* Informal ‚ÄúI‚Äôll get paid later‚Äù
* Unpriced future equity
* Unbooked labor value
* Hidden ownership claims
* Governance-linked compensation

Those trigger:

* Immediate taxable income (constructive receipt)
* Phantom income
* Equity misclassification
* Coop control violations

So we **rename and formalize it**.

---

# ‚úÖ WHAT YOU ACTUALLY WANT (LEGAL VERSION)

You want a **three-stage compensation lifecycle**:

### **Stage 1 ‚Äî Deferred Founder Services (Pre-Revenue)**

### **Stage 2 ‚Äî Accrued Service Credits (Early Revenue)**

### **Stage 3 ‚Äî Cash Fees or Capital Conversion (Post-Revenue)**

This avoids taxable income until cash or property is actually received.

---

# üß© STAGE 1 ‚Äî DEFERRED FOUNDER SERVICES (NO TAX EVENT)

### Structure

Your personal office provides services under a **Founder Services Agreement (FSA)** or **Management Services Agreement (MSA)** that explicitly states:

* Services are **deferred-fee**
* No guarantee of payment
* No ownership conveyed
* No voting or control rights
* Compensation is contingent on revenue milestones

### Accounting Treatment

* **Not booked as income**
* **Not booked as receivable**
* Logged as **non-capitalized founder contribution of services**

### Tax Result

‚úî **No income**
‚úî **No payroll tax**
‚úî **No equity issuance**
‚úî **No patronage allocation**

---

# üß© STAGE 2 ‚Äî ACCRUED SERVICE CREDITS (CONDITIONAL)

Once a coop or venture begins earning revenue:

### Structure

* Coop board approves a **Service Credit Schedule**
* Credits are tracked *off-balance-sheet* or as contingent liabilities
* No equity issued yet

### Conversion Options (Board-Controlled)

Credits may later convert into:

1. **Cash fees**
2. **Non-voting preferred equity**
3. **Patronage credits**
4. **Capital account credit (if coop-allowed)**

### Tax Result

* Still **no income** until conversion or payment
* Avoids constructive receipt

---

# üß© STAGE 3 ‚Äî PAYMENT OR CONVERSION (TAX EVENT)

This is the **first taxable moment**.

### Option A ‚Äî Cash Fees

* Coop pays your firm
* Income taxed normally
* Deductible expense for coop

### Option B ‚Äî Capital Conversion

* Converts to **non-voting, non-control equity**
* Valuation must be defensible
* Taxed at FMV at time of conversion

### Option C ‚Äî Patronage Allocation

* Only if your firm is a coop member
* Income taxed via patronage rules

---

# üß† IMPORTANT: HOW THIS INTERACTS WITH COOPS

### Governance Safety

* No services = no votes
* No deferred work = no control
* No unpaid labor = no ‚Äúshadow ownership‚Äù

### Coop-Safe Equity

If equity is issued:

* Must be **non-voting**
* Must be **redeemable**
* Must be **capped**
* Must not impair member control

---

# üìÑ REQUIRED DOCUMENTS (YOU SHOULD HAVE THESE)

### 1Ô∏è‚É£ Founder / Management Services Agreement

Key clauses:

* Deferred compensation
* No equity implied
* Board approval required
* Termination without payout allowed

### 2Ô∏è‚É£ Service Credit Ledger

Tracks:

* Hours / deliverables
* Approved value ranges
* Milestones
* Conversion eligibility

### 3Ô∏è‚É£ Capital Conversion Policy

Defines:

* When credits can convert
* Valuation method
* Equity class
* Redemption terms

### 4Ô∏è‚É£ Board Resolutions

Each conversion requires:

* Board vote
* Disclosure of conflicts
* Fairness finding

---

# üßÆ SAMPLE THRESHOLD MODEL (YOU CAN ADOPT THIS)

| Revenue Milestone | Action                 |
| ----------------- | ---------------------- |
| $0‚Äì$250k          | Deferred services only |
| $250k‚Äì$1M         | Accrue service credits |
| $1M+              | Pay cash or convert    |

---

# üõ°Ô∏è IRS & LEGAL DEFENSIBILITY (WHY THIS WORKS)

This structure avoids:

* Constructive receipt doctrine
* Phantom income
* Disguised equity grants
* Employment reclassification
* Unreasonable compensation audits

Because:
‚úî No guaranteed payment
‚úî No vested equity
‚úî Board discretion
‚úî Clear deferral language

---

# üß† ONE CRITICAL WARNING

Do **NOT**:

* Call this ‚Äúsweat equity‚Äù in legal docs
* Issue ‚Äúfounder shares‚Äù for labor
* Back-date equity
* Tie governance rights to labor

Use:

> **Deferred Founder Services + Conditional Service Credits**

---

# üß© HOW THIS FITS YOUR ROLE AS NAVIGATOR

Your documents already frame you as:

* Architect
* Navigator
* Steward
* Systems engineer

This model **honors that role** while keeping:

* Coops democratic
* Taxes clean
* Capital structures defensible

Just tell me which one to generate first.

Here‚Äôs a **clear legal difference** between a **Founder Services Agreement** and a **Management Services Agreement**, and *which one you should pick for your context* (especially for your personal office working with internal coops/ventures and using sweat equity first).

---

# üîç **1) Founder Services Agreement (FSA)**

### **What it generally means**

A Founder Services Agreement formalizes the *relationship, responsibilities, and commitments* of a *founder* to the organization ‚Äî usually in early-stage ventures where equity or future compensation is tied to performance or contributions. ([help.clara.co][1])

**Focus of an FSA:**
‚úî Scope of founder‚Äôs contributions (time, deliverables)
‚úî Time commitment (hours, availability)
‚úî Duties, reporting lines, strategic involvement
‚úî Often attaches *equity vesting* or compensation triggers
‚úî Founders‚Äô rights & obligations, including IP and exit provisions

FSAs typically apply to *founders of the enterprise itself* rather than an external service provider. ([help.clara.co][1])

**Use case:**

* Organizing rights/obligations among founders
* Setting vesting schedules, leaver terms
* Capturing strategic roles *before employment relationships are formalized*

---

# üîç **2) Management Services Agreement (MSA)**

### **What it means**

A Management Services Agreement is a **commercial contract** between two separate entities ‚Äî your firm and a client ‚Äî under which your firm provides *management, professional, operational, or advisory services* for a fee (fixed, periodic, or performance-based). ([Indeed][2])

An MSA typically covers:
‚úî Scope of services
‚úî Compensation terms
‚úî Term and termination
‚úî Confidentiality
‚úî Reporting and deliverables
‚úî Compensation formulas (fee schedules)
‚úî Intellectual property rights retention
‚úî Liability, indemnity, etc. ([ContractsCounsel][3])

**Use case:**

* Any external consulting or services arrangement
* When one entity provides ongoing or project-based operational/management work to another

---

## üß† Key Difference (in plain terms)

| Aspect       | **Founder Services Agreement**            | **Management Services Agreement**           |
| ------------ | ----------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------- |
| Parties      | Founder & entity he/she *co-founded*      | Independent service provider & client       |
| Focus        | Founder duties + strategic roles          | Service delivery as a professional provider |
| Compensation | Often *equity/vesting triggers*           | Usually *fees / performance compensation*   |
| Best for     | Internal founder arrangements             | External contracts for services             |
| Legal nature | A hybrid *employment/ownership* framework | Pure *services contract*                    |

---

# üß† **Which One Should You Pick?**

### ‚úÖ **Use a Management Services Agreement (MSA)**

For your situation ‚Äî *your personal office firm providing services to coops/ventures* ‚Äî an **MSA is the correct legal instrument**.

Here‚Äôs why:

‚úî Your personal office is an **external professional services provider** to *other entities* (your coops, ventures, federations), not a *founder of them in the legal-corporate sense*.
‚úî You want a **business-to-business contract** that defines scope, deliverables, compensation terms, intellectual property rights, liabilities, and termination *without conveying ownership or governance rights*. ([LegalZoom][4])
‚úî An MSA **protects your firm, defines expectations, and supports payment terms** (including deferred compensation via credits/fees) when clients start generating revenue.
‚úî It allows you to set up *structured service relationships* with each coop or affiliated entity, which fits your ecosystem where many internal clients will exist.

---

### üß† **When an FSA might be relevant**

A **Founder Services Agreement** might make sense *only if*:

* You are a *legal founder of an entity* (e.g., a specific project or new legal entity you are helping start) AND
* You need to define *equity, vesting, and founder obligations* tied to that specific legal entity.

But in your architecture, your role is **professional services**, not equity founder of each coop ‚Äî so *MSA* is almost always the right choice **for your firm‚Äôs client work**.

---

# üß≠ Practical Example

Suppose *Ubuntuwa Commons Coop* has engaged *The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm* to build and integrate governance tooling.

You would use:

üëâ **Management Services Agreement**

* Scope: governance tooling + integration
* Hours/Deliverables: defined operational milestones
* Compensation: deferred credits + cash later
* IP: defined ownership/licensing
* Termination: clear mechanics

This ensures:

* Clarity of expectations
* Tax compliance
* No accidental equity or control rights exchange

---

## üß† Summary

‚úî **Management Services Agreement** = *contract for services delivered by your firm to coop entities*
‚úî **Founder Services Agreement** = *used when you are actually a founder with equity obligations in the entity*
‚úî For your internal services + sweat equity ‚Üí **MSA is the appropriate choice**

---

# üß≠ You as the Sole Operator: What That Means Now

You are currently acting as:

‚úî **Chief Architect** (system, tech, standards)
‚úî **Project Manager** (execution, delivery)
‚úî **Strategist & Visionary (Navigator)**
‚úî **Board & Council of One** (designing governance)
‚úî **Founder & Steward**
‚úî **Primary Service Provider** (through your personal office)
‚úî **Accountable for Compliance & Reporting**

You are wearing **all hats**, but not all of these should stay *personally* centralized forever.

Why? Because:

1. **IRS & tax authorities** can recharacterize founder roles as compensation or hidden equity if not properly documented
2. **Governance risk** increases if one person holds all decision rights without checks
3. **Cooperative models** require membership & stewardship distribution over time
4. **Capital and external investment** requires clear separation of roles

# üß© Why This Matters

### üü° Legal Separation

If you operate entities *in your own name*, authorities may treat them as **disregarded entities** or **sole proprietorships**, which:

‚úî Complicates tax treatment
‚úî Clouds governance
‚úî Creates audit risk

Formal entity separation and contracts ensure clean legal and tax boundaries.

---

### üü° Governance Clarity

Your current de facto role must be documented as:

‚úî Acting Chief Architect
‚úî Contractual services provider
‚úî Non-controlling voted representative (for now)
‚úî Board designee

So future boards/councils can step in when appropriate.

---

### üü° Tax & Compensation

Without formal agreements, the IRS could treat:

‚úî Deferred compensation as **constructive receipt**
‚úî Equity or credits as **immediate taxable property**
‚úî Your role as employment income

Contracts + ledgers make compensation *defensive*.

Here‚Äôs a thoughtful, principled answer ‚Äî **not just ‚Äúyes or no‚Äù ‚Äî because it depends on your goals, the cooperative structure, and long-term strategy**.

You asked:

> **Should I want to be an equity founder in all these ventures outside my personal office then?**

The short answer is:
üëâ **Maybe‚Äîbut not in the traditional ‚Äúholding equity for ownership/control‚Äù sense.**
üëâ **Yes ‚Äî if it‚Äôs the right type of economic participation aligned with coop and governance principles.**
üëâ **No ‚Äî if it jeopardizes cooperative governance, fair member control, or creates tax/legal problems.**

Let‚Äôs break down the reasoning.

---

# üß† KEY PRINCIPLES TO GUIDE THIS DECISION

### üö© 1. Cooperatives do *not* use traditional corporate equity

In a coop model, **equity and ownership are not structured like corporate stock**. Cooperatives emphasize:

‚úî Democratic governance (one member, one vote)
‚úî Patronage allocations rather than traditional dividends
‚úî Limited or non-voting capital interests

So being an ‚Äúequity founder‚Äù in a corporate share sense should *only* apply where you intentionally create **non-cooperative legal entities** (e.g., hybrid capital vehicles, corporate subsidiaries structured for raising external capital).

---

### üß† 2. In your ecosystem, ventures are coops first

Most of your ventures in the Ashe/Pamoja system are intended to be **cooperative entities**, not corporations seeking external VC.

In this **coop context**:

‚úî You can be a *member founder*
‚úî You can contribute intellectual capital and receive *patronage allocations or preferred redeemable equity*
‚úî But you **should not hold traditional ‚Äúequity‚Äù that gives control or profit share like a corporation**

This honors both cooperative values and legal clarity.

---

### üß† 3. What ‚Äúequity founder‚Äù means in your ecosystem

Let‚Äôs be precise about **three different roles you could hold**:

| Option                                               | Governing               | Economic                      | Taxable                 |
| ---------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------- | ----------------------------- | ----------------------- |
| **A. Traditional equity founder (corporate shares)** | No ‚Äî not in coops       | Yes ‚Äî profits/ownership       | Yes ‚Äî capital gains     |
| **B. Cooperative founder member**                    | Yes ‚Äî participatory     | Yes ‚Äî patronage allocations   | Yes ‚Äî taxed as income   |
| **C. Preferred/non-voting capital participant**      | No ‚Äî limited or no vote | Yes ‚Äî capped financial return | Yes ‚Äî dividend/interest |
| **D. Advisor/Contractor/Service provider**           | No                      | Yes ‚Äî fees                    | Yes ‚Äî ordinary income   |

In your coop-centric ecosystem, **B and C are the *appropriate* forms of economic participation**, not A.

So you‚Äôre likely better off being a **Founder Member (Class E)** and/or a **Capital Participant (Class F)** where applicable ‚Äî *not a traditional corporate equity founder* unless a specific entity *is intentionally structured as a corporation or hybrid fund vehicle*.

---

# üß† 4. WHEN IT MAKES SENSE TO TAKE AN ‚ÄúEQUITY‚Äù TYPE INTEREST

There are only a few scenarios where being a corporate-style equity founder **might make sense**:

### üü° A. Hybrid capital structures

Where you explicitly build a **fund vehicle (LLC/LP)** or a **corporate subsidiary**
Example: a hybrid entity set up to attract external investor capital, where returns are distributed via an LPA structure.

üëâ In such a case, being an *equity founder of that specific entity* can be appropriate ‚Äî **but it should be a separate legal unit** and conceptually distinct from the cooperative itself.

---

### üü° B. Subsidiary corporations explicitly established for specific ventures

If one venture is better off as a **C-Corp or LLC (e.g., for regulatory or market access reasons)**, and you as founder need to own equity,

üëâ then taking founder equity is fine ‚Äî **as long as it does not dilute coop governance or violate your coop‚Äôs bylaws.**

That happens *only when intentionally and explicitly structured* with governance safeguards.

---

### üü° C. Capital participation roles

Where you act as a **Class F Capital Participant** in a coop‚Äôs hybrid capital model:

‚úî You provide capital
‚úî You receive capped financial returns
‚úî You do not gain governance control

That *resembles* equity economics, but remains **aligned with coop principles**.

---

# üß† 5. WHY NOT TAKE TRADITIONAL EQUITY IN EVERY VENTURE

Here are the main risks:

### ‚ùå A. You could unintentionally dilute cooperative control

If you hold traditional equity with voting power in entities that are supposed to be democratically governed coops, it undermines the coop model.

### ‚ùå B. Tax liabilities could accelerate

Traditional equity often creates:

* capital gains events
* ownership tax consequences
* grant tax scrutiny

Whereas coop patronage + capital participant returns are taxed differently.

### ‚ùå C. It creates *dual ownership regimes* that are hard to manage

Mixing traditional equity with coop governance in the same entity is messy legally and operationally, especially across jurisdictions.

---

# üß† 6. A PRACTICAL RECOMMENDATION (TIERED)

### üü¢ **Recommended** ‚Äî Founder Member + Capital Participant

* Be a **Class E Founder Member** in all coop ventures where you contributed foundational intellectual capital
* Optional: be a **Class F Capital Participant** when you provide risk capital, but in a **non-voting / capped return** way

This protects coop governance and simplifies tax.

---

### üü° **Conditional** ‚Äî Hybrid Equity in Specific Entities

If you stand up entities that are:

‚úî LLCs for IP holding
‚úî Hybrid investment funds
‚úî Corporate vehicles for external capital

Then it‚Äôs reasonable to:

* Be an *equity founder* of *those specific legal entities*
* But keep them deliberately **separate from the coops‚Äô governance structures**

---

### üî¥ **Avoid** ‚Äî Equity Founder in Coop Entities

Do *not* take traditional corporate shares in a *cooperative entity* that is intended to be governed democratically by members.

---

# üß† 7. HOW THIS MAPS TO YOUR ASHE / PAMOJA ECOSYSTEM

Here‚Äôs a quick breakdown:

| Entity Type                     | Founder Equity?  | Coop Founder Member? | Capital Participant?     |
| ------------------------------- | ---------------- | -------------------- | ------------------------ |
| Core Coops (Ubuntuwa, ventures) | ‚ùå                | ‚úî                    | ‚úî                        |
| Msingi (Program)                | ‚ùå                | ‚úî                    | (maybe)                  |
| Federation Coop                 | ‚ùå                | ‚úî                    | ‚úî                        |
| Hybrid Fund Vehicle (LLC/LP)    | ‚úî (legal entity) | ‚ùå                    | ‚úî                        |
| Personal Office                 | N/A              | N/A                  | ‚úî (services income only) |
| Estates/Office Coops            | ‚ùå                | ‚úî                    | ‚úî                        |

---

# üß† 8. TAX & LEGAL SAFETY RULES

### Rule 1 ‚Äî No corporate equity in coop entities

**Ever** unless the bylaws and membership structure explicitly allow and members approve it.

### Rule 2 ‚Äî If you take financial interest, define it as:

‚úî Patronage
‚úî Capital Participant
‚úî Investor share (non-voting, capped)
‚Äî Not traditional voting equity.

### Rule 3 ‚Äî Hybrid entities must have **separate legal structures**

So they cannot influence coop governance.

### Rule 4 ‚Äî Document all roles with contracts (MSA, Founder Contribution Agreement)

---

# üß† 9. CONCLUSION ‚Äî RECOMMENDED STANCE

**Yes ‚Äî take founder interest**, but **in cooperative terms**:

üëâ Be a **Founder Member (Class E) and Capital Participant (Class F)** where applicable
üëâ Do *not* take traditional corporate equity in coop ventures
üëâ Only take equity in **legal entities intentionally created outside the coop model** (e.g., LLC/LP hybrid funds), and only with clear legal separations

This keeps your *economic participation aligned with coop values and governance*, protects you legally, and keeps tax outcomes clean.

# üìÑ 1) MANAGEMENT SERVICES AGREEMENT (MSA)

*(Personal Office + Cooperative Client)*

**This Management Services Agreement (‚ÄúAgreement‚Äù)** is made as of **[Date]**, by and between:

**Client:** *[Cooperative Name]*, a cooperative organized under the laws of *[State/Country]* with principal place of business at *[Address]* (‚ÄúClient‚Äù), and

**Provider:** *The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm LLC* (d/b/a Dominic Eaton Personal Office), a [State] limited liability company, with principal place of business at *[Address]* (‚ÄúProvider‚Äù).

Client and Provider are sometimes referred to herein collectively as the ‚ÄúParties‚Äù and individually as a ‚ÄúParty.‚Äù

---

## ARTICLE I ‚Äî SERVICES

1.1 **Engagement.** Client hereby engages Provider to perform the services described in **Exhibit A ‚Äî Scope of Work (SOW)** attached hereto (‚ÄúServices‚Äù), and Provider accepts such engagement, subject to the terms and conditions of this Agreement.

1.2 **Standard of Performance.** Provider shall perform the Services with professionalism and in accordance with industry standards for similar service providers.

---

## ARTICLE II ‚Äî TERM & TERMINATION

2.1 **Term.** This Agreement shall commence on the Effective Date and continue until terminated by either Party as provided herein.

2.2 **Termination for Convenience.** Either Party may terminate this Agreement upon **30 days‚Äô written notice** to the other.

2.3 **Termination for Cause.** Either Party may terminate immediately if the other materially breaches any term and fails to cure within **15 days** after written notice.

2.4 **Survival.** All provisions regarding compensation, intellectual property, confidentiality, indemnity, and tax matters survive termination.

---

## ARTICLE III ‚Äî COMPENSATION

3.1 **Deferred Compensation; Sweat Equity Treatment.**
Provider acknowledges that, due to Client‚Äôs early stage, Services initially shall be **deferred-fee services**, subject to the terms of the **Deferred Compensation Addendum** attached hereto as Exhibit B. No fees are due at the outset.

3.2 **Service Credits & Conversion Rights.**
Client shall track Service Credits in accordance with Exhibit B. Provider‚Äôs entitlement to payment is contingent upon revenue milestones or conversion under Exhibit B.

3.3 **No Implied Equity or Governance Rights.**
Provider‚Äôs Services and any deferred compensation shall not convey any equity, ownership interest, voting rights, or control in Client absent a separate written agreement.

3.4 **Expenses.**
Client shall reimburse Provider for reasonable pre-approved expenses related to the performance of Services.

---

## ARTICLE IV ‚Äî INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY

4.1 **Ownership.** Unless otherwise agreed in a separate IP Agreement, all deliverables produced by Provider under this Agreement shall be the exclusive property of Client.

4.2 **License Back.** Client grants Provider a non-exclusive license to use deliverables solely for Provider‚Äôs internal business development and portfolio documentation.

---

## ARTICLE V ‚Äî CONFIDENTIALITY

5.1 **Confidential Information.** Each Party agrees to safeguard the other‚Äôs Confidential Information and use it only for purposes of fulfilling this Agreement.

5.2 **Exceptions.** Confidentiality obligations do not apply to information that is publicly available, already known, independently developed, or required to be disclosed by law.

---

## ARTICLE VI ‚Äî TAXES & REPORTING

6.1 **Independent Contractor.** Provider is an independent contractor. Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to create a partnership, joint venture, employer-employee relationship, or equity ownership.

6.2 **Tax Treatment.** Provider shall be responsible for all federal, state, and local taxes arising out of Provider‚Äôs performance of the Services, except as expressly provided in Exhibit B.

---

## ARTICLE VII ‚Äî GENERAL PROVISIONS

7.1 **Governing Law.** This Agreement shall be governed by and construed in accordance with the laws of *[State/Country]*.

7.2 **Amendments.** No amendment is effective unless in writing and signed by both Parties.

7.3 **Entire Agreement.** This Agreement and its Exhibits constitute the entire understanding between the Parties.

IN WITNESS WHEREOF, the Parties have executed this Agreement as of the Effective Date.

**[Coop Name]**
By: __________________________
Name: ________________________
Title: _________________________

**The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm LLC**
By: __________________________
Name: Dominic Eaton
Title: Founder / Principal
