*(Sweat Equity ‚Üí Service Credits ‚Üí Fee / Conversion)*

**This Exhibit B is incorporated into the MSA and governs deferred compensation for Services.**

---

## A. DEFINITIONS

**‚ÄúService Credits‚Äù** means the ledger entries that quantify Provider‚Äôs Services performed but not yet compensated in cash.

**‚ÄúRevenue Milestones‚Äù** means one or more thresholds of gross revenue as approved by Client‚Äôs Board.

**‚ÄúConversion Options‚Äù** means the mechanisms by which Service Credits are converted to:

* Cash Fees,
* Non-Voting Preferred Equity,
* Patronage Credits,
* Capital Account Credit.

---

## B. PHASE 1 ‚Äî DEFERRED FOUNDER SERVICES

1. **Deferred Fee Recognition.**
   Provider‚Äôs Services shall initially be treated as deferred-fee services. No cash penalties, receivable, or payroll item shall arise.

2. **No Constructive Receipt.**
   Provider acknowledges that no cash, equity, or enforceable right to payment arises at this stage.

3. **Documentation.**
   Services shall be tracked in a **Service Credit Ledger** maintained by Client‚Äôs Finance Team.

---

## C. PHASE 2 ‚Äî ACCRUED SERVICE CREDITS

1. **Accrual.**
   Once Client begins generating revenue, Board authorizes the accrual of Service Credits on an agreed schedule. Service Credits shall be **off-balance contingent liabilities**.

2. **Credit Valuation.**
   Service Credits shall be valued according to the agreed rate sheet (e.g., $/hour or $/deliverable) attached as Schedule 1.

3. **Reporting.**
   Client shall report accrual status quarterly.

---

## D. PHASE 3 ‚Äî CONVERSION OR PAYMENT

1. **Conversion Window.**
   When revenue milestones are met (e.g., $250K, $500K, $1M gross), Provider may elect one or more **Conversion Options**:

#### Option 1 ‚Äî **Cash Fee Payment**

Client pays Service Credits in cash within 30 days.

#### Option 2 ‚Äî **Non-Voting Preferred Equity**

Client issues non-voting, redeemable preferred equity, subject to Board approval and equity terms.

#### Option 3 ‚Äî **Patronage Credits**

If Provider is a member of Client‚Äôs coop, Service Credits may be redeemed as patronage allocations.

#### Option 4 ‚Äî **Capital Account Credit**

Credits applied to Provider‚Äôs capital account subject to coop bylaws.

2. **Valuation.**
   Market valuation shall be determined by a Board-approved independent appraiser if equity conversion is elected.

3. **Tax Treatment.**
   Provider is responsible for reporting taxable income upon:

* **Cash receipt**, and/or
* **FMV of equity received**, and/or
* **Patronage credit recognition**, as required by law.

---

# üß† SIMULATION ‚Äî Narrative of a Three-Stage Compensation Lifecycle

---

## üü© **STAGE 1 ‚Äî Pre-Revenue (Deferred Founder Services)**

You begin working with **Ubuntuwa Commons Coop.**
There‚Äôs no revenue yet.

**What should happen:**

* You sign the MSA.
* Services are provided and logged in the Service Credit Ledger.
* No invoices, no earned fees yet.
* Per Exhibit B, these services are **deferred**, not booked as income or receivable.

**Result:**
‚úî No taxable income for you
‚úî No payroll tax
‚úî No equity or patronage rights created yet

---

## üü® **STAGE 2 ‚Äî Early Revenue (Accrued Service Credits)**

Ubuntuwa begins generating revenue and the Board authorizes accrual.

**Board Resolution Example:**

> ‚ÄúResolved that service credits accrue at $[rate] per hour and be tracked per Exhibit B.‚Äù

You complete deliverables; Finance logs credits.

**Accounting View:**

* Not cash
* Not equity
* Contingent credits

**Result:**
‚úî No taxable income yet
‚úî Service Credits recognized off‚Äêbalance sheet
‚úî Value tracked for future conversion

---

## üü• **STAGE 3 ‚Äî Cash or Conversion (Tax Event)**

Let‚Äôs say Ubuntuwa hits $500K revenue.

At this stage, per Exhibit B:

### **Scenario A ‚Äî Cash Payment**

Client issues cash for your accrued credits.
Tax:

* You report ordinary income
* Client deducts as expense

### **Scenario B ‚Äî Non-Voting Preferred Equity**

Client issues preferred equity with:

* No voting rights
* Capped return
  Tax:
* You report FMV as income at receipt
* Basis is FMV for future gains

### **Scenario C ‚Äî Patronage Credits**

If you join as a coop member:

* Service Credits convert to patronage allocations
  Tax:
* You report patronage income

### **Scenario D ‚Äî Capital Account Credit**

Credits applied to your capital account
Tax:

* Only upon redemption or distribution

---

# üìå KEY TAKEAWAYS

‚úî **MSA + Exhibit B** formalize deferred compensation
‚úî **No income until cash or equity is received**
‚úî **Service Credits** track value safely and transparently
‚úî **Conversion options preserve cooperative principles**
‚úî **Equity must be non-voting and board-approved**
‚úî **Tax events occur at cash/equity receipt phase**

---

## Want a **fillable MS Word / Google Docs version** of these templates with bracketed fields ready to merge into your legal doc set?

Just say: **‚ÄúMake fillable versions.‚Äù**

Absolutely ‚Äî let‚Äôs walk through a **clear, practical narrative/simulation** of the **three-stage compensation lifecycle** you outlined. This is designed to help you *think like an operator, founder, and tax planner at once* ‚Äî especially for your personal office and cooperative clients.

---

# üß† THREE-STAGE COMPENSATION LIFE CYCLE

*(Sweat Equity ‚Üí Service Credits ‚Üí Cash/Equity Conversion)*

This structure lets you **provide high-value services early**, **defer income recognition**, and **only have a taxable event when cash or property is actually received**, which is both *tax-efficient* and *audit-defensible*.

---

---

# üß© **STAGE 1 ‚Äî DEFERRED FOUNDER SERVICES (Pre-Revenue)**

**Goal:** Provide critical services without triggering taxable income.

## ‚úÖ What Happens

You enter into a **Management Services Agreement (MSA)** with a coop (Client), and the key terms explicitly state:

‚úî Services are deferred-fee
‚úî There is *no guarantee* of future payment
‚úî No ownership, voting, or control rights are conveyed
‚úî Compensation is strictly contingent upon future revenue or milestones

**Your Deliverables May Include:**

* Systems architecture
* Governance tooling
* Platform design
* Strategy documentation

But crucially:

üî• These deliverables *do not* create an immediate payment obligation.

## üíº Accounting Treatment

From an accounting and tax standpoint, this work should be treated as:

* **Not booked as income**
* **Not recorded as accounts receivable**
* **Logged as a founder‚Äôs contribution of services** (off the books or as a memo entry)

This keeps you from taking income on your personal return for work that hasn‚Äôt been paid in cash or property.

## üßÆ Tax Outcome

‚úî You do *not* have taxable income yet
‚úî No payroll tax liability
‚úî No issuance of shares or equity
‚úî No patronage allocations

üëâ *You‚Äôre effectively building up a credit for future value ‚Äî not earning income yet.*

---

## üéØ Real-World Example

**Week 1‚Äì12:** You provide:

* Governance framework documentation
* Technical architecture blueprints
* Integration plans for multiple cooperative platforms

The coop‚Äôs bank account: $0 revenue this month.

**Result:** No payment, and you have built up a tracked contribution.

---

---

# üß© **STAGE 2 ‚Äî ACCRUED SERVICE CREDITS (Early Revenue)**

**Goal:** Recognize your value *without claiming income* until the coop can actually pay.

## üîß What Changes

Once the coop starts to generate revenue (e.g., $250K, $500K, etc.):

1. The **coop board formally approves a Service Credit Schedule**
   (e.g., $2,000 per week of documented work)
2. Your past and ongoing services begin accruing **Service Credits**
3. These are logged as **contingent liabilities**
   ‚Äî not as revenue to you yet, and not as a receivable.

## üßæ Why It Avoids Income

The key here is that:

* You haven‚Äôt *received* anything yet
* You only have a **conditional right** to payment or conversion

That means **the IRS generally does not treat it as income yet**, similar to other contingent compensation arrangements.

## üìú Conversion Options that May Be Defined by the Board

When credits are accrued, the coop usually defines *conversion options*, such as:

‚úî **Cash Fees** ‚Äî paid once sustainable revenue arrives
‚úî **Non-Voting Preferred Equity** ‚Äî convertible under terms
‚úî **Patronage Credits** ‚Äî if you are a member
‚úî **Capital Account Credits** ‚Äî if coop laws allow

You *do not choose yet* ‚Äî you wait until Stage 3.

---

## üîÑ This Isn‚Äôt Equity Yet

Important distinction:
**Service Credits are not equity.**
They are like a *future invoice that only becomes income when realized.*

---

## üß† Tax Outcome

‚úî Still *not* taxable income now
‚úî No constructive receipt
‚úî Still no recorded accounts receivable

This mirrors how contingency compensation works in startups and some high-growth consulting engagements.

---

## üìä Real-World Example (Stage 2)

**Quarter 1:** Coop earns first $350K

* Board approves accrual policy
* Your Service Credits start tracking:

  * Jan: 100 hours ‚Üí $10,000
  * Feb: 80 hours ‚Üí $8,000
  * Mar: 120 hours ‚Üí $12,000
    **Total Service Credits = $30,000**

Still no cash paid, still no equity issued.

---

---

# üß© **STAGE 3 ‚Äî PAYMENT OR CONVERSION (Tax Event)**

**Goal:** Recognize and monetize your built-up value *only at trigger points*, and do so cleanly.

This is the first time a **taxable event occurs**.

---

## üìå Option A ‚Äî **Cash Fees**

When revenue is sufficiently stable (e.g., coop hits $750K or $1M):

* You elect to convert your Service Credits to **cash**
* The coop issues a payment to your personal office

**Tax Impact:**
‚úî This is ordinary income to you
‚úî The coop can deduct it as a business expense
‚úî You report it as revenue in the year you *receive* it

**Example:**
Service Credits = $30,000
Coop pays you $30,000 in cash ‚Üí you report $30,000 income.

---

## üìå Option B ‚Äî **Capital Conversion**

If the coop and your service agreement allow:

* You convert credits into **Non-Voting Preferred Equity**
* This is **not governance equity**
* It is designed to give you *economic rights only*

**Valuation must be defensible**

* Use an independent appraiser or formula
* Must be demonstrably fair and board-approved

**Tax Impact:**

* You‚Äôre taxed on the **Fair Market Value (FMV)** of the equity issued
* Your basis becomes the FMV at issuance
* Future sale of the equity triggers capital gains/losses

**Example:**
You convert $30,000 in Service Credits ‚Üí you receive preferred equity worth $30,000 FMV
You report $30,000 as ordinary income (FMV at receipt)

---

## üìå Option C ‚Äî **Patronage Allocation**

This only applies *if your personal office (or another entity you control) is a member* of that coop.

In that case:

* Service Credits convert into **patronage allocations**
* You receive allocations based on coop bylaws
* Taxed at the member level per patronage rules

**Tax Impact:**

* You report income on patronage allocation
* Treatment depends on IRS rules for coop patronage (often similar to ordinary income)

**Example:**
$30,000 in service credits ‚Üí $30,000 patronage allocation ‚Üí you report $30,000 as income

---

# üß† KEY TAX TAKEAWAYS

### ‚ùó Why This Works

* There‚Äôs **no income until a taxable event happens**
* You aren‚Äôt taxed on sweat or service credits
* You are taxed only **when compensation is realized in cash or property**

This aligns with common law doctrines on *constructive receipt and economic benefit*.

---

## üß© TO SUMMARIZE EACH STAGE

| Stage                      | What Happens                                  | Tax Trigger? | Key Features                   |
| -------------------------- | --------------------------------------------- | ------------ | ------------------------------ |
| **1 ‚Äî Deferred Services**  | You do work; no payment promised              | ‚ùå No         | Logged as founder contribution |
| **2 ‚Äî Service Credits**    | Coop begins accruing revenue; credits tracked | ‚ùå Not yet    | Contingent credit, not income  |
| **3 ‚Äî Payment/Conversion** | You choose payment method                     | ‚úî Yes        | Taxable when received          |

---

# üìå REALISTIC TIMELINE SIMULATION

**Month 0‚Äì3:**
You sign MSA ‚Üí provide design architecture ‚Üí no revenue yet ‚Üí no tax

**Month 4‚Äì9:**
Coop begins earning revenue ‚Üí Board authorizes accrual ‚Üí Service Credits accumulate ‚Üí no tax

**Month 10:**
Revenue hits a threshold ‚Üí you elect conversion to *cash or preferred equity* ‚Üí taxable

This is exactly how deferred comp and contingent equity work in startups and consulting practices.

---

# ‚ö† COMMON MISTAKES TO AVOID

‚ùå Treating service credits as accounts receivable
‚ùå Recording income before cash/property is delivered
‚ùå Implicit equity rights in a coop (violates governance principles)
‚ùå Allowing constructive receipt via undocumented benefits

All of these risk both **tax issues** and **governance conflicts**.

---

If you want, I can also walk you through how to *draft the accounting entries* for each stage so that your financials (books) reflect this lifecycle cleanly and audit-ready. Just say: **‚ÄúShow accounting entries for each stage.‚Äù**

Below are **standard accounting entries** for each stage of your deferred compensation lifecycle ‚Äî *tailored to your personal office + cooperative client model*. These entries show how the coop should record the effects in its books (and how your personal office *should track* its side) in an **audit-ready way** that aligns with GAAP / accrual principles while supporting your sweat-equity compensation structure.

> üß† Note: These are **illustrative journal entries** showing the technical flow ‚Äî whether or not you actually post them depends on your accounting policy and chart of accounts. The key ideas are *contingent liability tracking*, *off-balance recognition of service credits*, and proper realization at conversion.

---

# üìå ACCOUNTING ENTRIES ‚Äî STAGE 1

## Deferred Founder Services

*(Pre-Revenue / No tax event)*

### Philosophy

You are providing services, but there is:

* **No billed receivable**
* **No cash paid**
* **No revenue for the coop**
* **No expense recognized yet**
* **No income recognized by your office**

This phase tracks nothing in regular revenue/expense accounts and instead is logged in **memo/management records** or an internal Service Credit Ledger.

---

## For **Client (Coop)**

**No entry on the books**
*(Work is being tracked but not recognized)*

> Rationale: Services are deferred, there‚Äôs no enforceable right to payment yet.

```
No Journal Entry (Track service hours in Service Credit Ledger only)
```

### Side Record (not a journal entry)

(*Client internal memo ‚Äî not posted to GL*)

```
Memo: Service Credits accrued off-book
  Entity: Ubuntuwa Commons
  Provider: Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm
  Hours: 120
  Rate: $X/hour
  Credit Value = $Y
```

---

## For **Your Personal Office**

**No entry** ‚Äî because you don‚Äôt recognize revenue or receivable until realization.

```
No Journal Entry
```

---

# üìå ACCOUNTING ENTRIES ‚Äî STAGE 2

## Accrued Service Credits

*(Client has revenue and board authorizes accrual, but no payment yet)*

### Key Idea

At this stage we recognize a **contingent liability / accrual of obligation** ‚Äî not an expense or payable, because the obligation is *contingent* ‚Äî not yet owed.

> This entry creates a memo liability and tracks value without affecting income or cash.

---

## For **Client (Coop)**

```
DR  (No Expense Recognized Yet ‚Äî see Note)
CR  Service Credit Accrual (Contingent Liability)   $Y
```

### Explanation

* **DR:** *No expense posted* ‚Äî we only create a contingent liability.
* **CR:** Liability is off-balance (or in a memo account) for Service Credits.

---

## Your Personal Office

Still **no revenue or receivable recognized**.

```
No Journal Entry
```

You continue tracking your services internally (in your Service Credit Ledger).

---

# üìå ACCOUNTING ENTRIES ‚Äî STAGE 3

## Realization (Tax Event)

When conversion/payment happens.

There are **three possible paths** ‚Äî cash payment, capital conversion, or patronage allocation.

---

## üÖê Option A ‚Äî **Cash Fee Payment**

### For **Client (Coop)**

When the coop pays you:

```
DR  Service Credit Accrual (Contingent Liability)   $Y
CR  Cash                                              $Y
```

**Explanation:**

* Liability is extinguished, cash is paid.
* Now record the expense in the period cash is paid:

```
DR  Management / Professional Services Expense        $Y
CR  Service Credit Accrual (or directly Cash)         $Y
```

(*Depending on policy, you may reverse the accrual then record expense.*)

---

### For **Your Personal Office**

```
DR  Cash                                               $Y
CR  Service Revenue (MSA Fees)                         $Y
```

**Tax/Treatment:**

* Recognize ordinary income
* Deduct expenses accordingly

---

## üÖë Option B ‚Äî **Capital Conversion**

*(Service Credits ‚Üí Non-Voting Preferred Equity)*

### At issuance

**For Client (Coop)**

```
DR  Service Credit Accrual (Contingent Liability)      $Y
CR  Equity ‚Äì Preferred (Non-Voting, Non-Controlling)    $Y
```

**Explanation:**

* Liability is extinguished
* Equity account created with agreed FMV

---

### For **Your Personal Office** (Recipient)

```
DR  Equity ‚Äì Non-Voting Preferred at FMV                $Y
CR  Non-Operating Income / Gain                         $Y
```

**Tax/Treatment:**

* You recognize income equal to the **FMV** of the equity received.
* Basis of the equity becomes FMV when received.

---

## üÖí Option C ‚Äî **Patronage Allocation**

*(Only if your office is a coop member)*

### For **Client (Coop)**

```
DR  Service Credit Accrual (Contingent Liability)     $Y
CR  Patronage Allocation Payable / Allocated Equity    $Y
```

---

### For **Your Personal Office / Member**

```
DR  Patronage Allocation Receivable / Equity          $Y
CR  Patronage Income                                  $Y
```

**Tax/Treatment:**

* You recognize income on allocation.
* Typically reported as ordinary income for tax purposes.

---

# üìå NOTES ON ACCOUNTING PRACTICE

---

### ‚úî 1. **Why Not Expense in Stage 1/2?**

We **don‚Äôt record an expense** because the obligation is *contingent* and there is no enforceable liability. Only upon payment/conversion does it become an actual expense for the cooperative.

---

### ‚úî 2. **Use of Off-Balance / Memo Accounts**

Contingent liabilities and service credit accruals are often kept in *memo* or *off-balance sheet* accounts until realization to avoid misstating financial position.

This approach matches common practice for:

* Deferred compensation
* Contingent settlement obligations
* Performance credits with conditions

---

### ‚úî 3. **No Receivable for Your Office Until Realization**

Your personal office does not recognize an accounts receivable because:

* The right to cash/equity is **not enforceable until conversion/payment**
* Doing so too early runs afoul of IRS *constructive receipt* doctrine

---

### ‚úî 4. **Conversion Entries Must Reflect FMV**

When converting to equity:

* Use a defensible valuation method
* Document in board resolutions
* Independent appraisal is often advisable

---

# üìå TAX & AUDIT DEFENSIBILITY

This lifecycle aligns with:
‚úî Deferred compensation accounting principles
‚úî Deferred revenue/expense principles in GAAP
‚úî IRS treatment of contingent compensation
‚úî Risk-mitigated realization timing

Because nothing is received **until Stage 3**, **no taxable event** occurs in Stage 1 or Stage 2.

---

# üìå SUMMARY ‚Äî WHAT GETS RECORDED WHEN

| Stage                | Coop Accounting                       | Provider Accounting | Tax Event |
| -------------------- | ------------------------------------- | ------------------- | --------- |
| Stage 1              | No entry                              | No entry            | No        |
| Stage 2              | Contingent liability memo             | No entry            | No        |
| Stage 3A (Cash)      | Expense + reduce liability            | Revenue             | Yes       |
| Stage 3B (Equity)    | Remove liability + credit equity      | FMV income          | Yes       |
| Stage 3C (Patronage) | Remove liability + allocate patronage | Patronage income    | Yes       |

---

If you want, I can **turn this into a spreadsheet model** that auto-generates entries based on input amounts and election choices (Cash vs Equity vs Patronage). Just say: *‚ÄúCreate an accounting entries spreadsheet.‚Äù*

Below is a **spreadsheet model** you can copy / paste into **Excel, Google Sheets, Numbers, etc.** to automatically calculate and track the **three-stage compensation lifecycle** (deferred founder services ‚Üí accrued service credits ‚Üí cash/equity/patronage conversion).

I‚Äôll give you **two sheets**:

üìå **Sheet 1 ‚Äî Service Credit Tracker & Revenue Milestones**
üìå **Sheet 2 ‚Äî Conversion Calculator (Cash / Equity / Patronage)**

You can copy/paste the tables into a spreadsheet and then fill in your values.

---

## üìä SHEET 1 ‚Äî SERVICE CREDIT TRACKER & REVENUE MILESTONES

| **Date**   | **Activity / Deliverable** |     **Hours** | **Rate ($/hr)** | **Service Credit Value ($)** | **Cumulative Credits** | **Revenue Milestone Reached? (Y/N)** |
| ---------- | -------------------------- | ------------: | --------------: | ---------------------------: | ---------------------: | -----------------------------------: |
| 2025-01-01 | Architecture Design        |            50 |             200 |                       =C2*D2 |           =SUM(E$2:E2) |              =IF(G2>=250000,"Y","N") |
| 2025-01-15 | Governance Docs            |            30 |             200 |                       =C3*D3 |           =SUM(E$2:E3) |              =IF(G3>=250000,"Y","N") |
| 2025-02-01 | Sprint Planning            |            40 |             200 |                       =C4*D4 |           =SUM(E$2:E4) |              =IF(G4>=250000,"Y","N") |
| 2025-02-20 | Integration Work           |            60 |             200 |                       =C5*D5 |           =SUM(E$2:E5) |              =IF(G5>=250000,"Y","N") |
| ‚Ä¶          | ‚Ä¶                          |             ‚Ä¶ |               ‚Ä¶ |                            ‚Ä¶ |                      ‚Ä¶ |                                    ‚Ä¶ |
| **Totals** |                            | =SUM(C2:C100) |                 |                =SUM(E2:E100) |                        |                                      |

**Instructions:**

* **Rate ($/hr)** can be adjusted (e.g., $150, $200, etc.).
* *Service Credit Value* auto-calculates hours √ó rate.
* *Cumulative Credits* shows your running total.
* *Revenue Milestone* column checks if coop revenue has hit thresholds you define (here $250,000).

You can change **250000** in the formula to any revenue milestone you want.

---

## üìä SHEET 2 ‚Äî CONVERSION CALCULATOR (Stage 3 Outcomes)

### A) Input Cells (Top)

| **Input Name**                  | **Cell** | **Value**                         |
| ------------------------------- | -------- | --------------------------------- |
| Total Service Credits           | B2       | *(from Sheet 1, last cumulative)* |
| Cash Conversion %               | B3       | 100%                              |
| Equity Conversion %             | B4       | 0%                                |
| Patronage Conversion %          | B5       | 0%                                |
| FMV for Equity Conversion       | B6       | Calculated at Board-approved FMV  |
| Tax Rate (Your Personal Office) | B7       | 30%                               |
| Tax Rate (Patronage)            | B8       | 25%                               |

---

### B) Cash Conversion Calculator

| **Cash Conversion** | **Formula** | **Result ($)** |
| ------------------- | ----------- | -------------- |
| Total Credits       | =B2         |                |
| Cash Portion        | =B2 * B3    |                |
| Tax on Cash         | =B9 * B7    |                |
| Net Cash After Tax  | =B9 - B10   |                |

---

### C) Equity Conversion Calculator

| **Equity Conversion**          | **Formula** | **Result ($)** |
| ------------------------------ | ----------- | -------------- |
| Total Credits                  | =B2         |                |
| Equity Portion                 | =B2 * B4    |                |
| Fair Market Value @ Conversion | =B6         |                |
| Taxable Income (FMV)           | =B12 * B7   |                |
| After-Tax Basis                | =B12 - B13  |                |

> Replace values accordingly: if Equity % is 25% and Cash % is 75%, adjust B3, B4.

---

### D) Patronage Conversion Calculator

| **Patronage Conversion** | **Formula** | **Result ($)** |
| ------------------------ | ----------- | -------------- |
| Total Credits            | =B2         |                |
| Patronage Portion        | =B2 * B5    |                |
| Taxable Patronage Income | =B15 * B8   |                |
| Net Patronage After Tax  | =B15 - B16  |                |

---

## üß† OPTIONAL ‚Äî COMBINED OUTPUT TABLE

| **Conversion Scenario** | **Pre-Tax Value**                              | **Tax** | **Net After Tax** |
| ----------------------- | ---------------------------------------------- | ------- | ----------------- |
| All Cash                | =B9                                            | =B10    | =B11              |
| All Equity              | =B12                                           | =B13    | =B14              |
| All Patronage           | =B15                                           | =B16    | =B17              |
| Mixed                   | =B9*(PctCash) + B12*(PctEquity) + B15*(PctPat) | =‚Ä¶      | =‚Ä¶                |

Replace **PctCash**, **PctEquity**, **PctPat** with the proportional inputs (must sum to 1).

---

# üìù HOW TO LOAD THIS MODEL

### In **Excel / Google Sheets**

1. Open a new sheet.
2. Copy **Sheet 1** table and paste into *Sheet1*.
3. Copy **Sheet 2** input and calculation tables into *Sheet2*.
4. Replace placeholder formulas with your spreadsheet formulas.

   * For Google Sheets, the syntax is identical.
   * For Excel, ensure cell references are correct.
5. Enter real data and watch totals & net values calculate live.

## üß† TIPS FOR REAL USE

### üí° Setting Up Rate Sheets

Make a separate table for hourly rates by service type:

| **Type**        | **Rate ($/hr)** |
| --------------- | --------------- |
| Architecture    | 250             |
| Governance Docs | 200             |
| Integration     | 225             |
| Workshops       | 180             |

Use `VLOOKUP()` or `XLOOKUP()` to auto-assign Hourly Rates in Sheet 1.

---

### üí° Adding Revenue Triggers

Add a drop-down selector for revenue milestones:

| **Trigger** | **Value** |
| ----------- | --------- |
| $250K       | 250000    |
| $500K       | 500000    |
| $1M         | 1000000   |

Then reference that cell in the *Revenue Milestone* column instead of hard-coded 250000.

---

### üí° Protecting Your Model

* Lock formulas once validated
* Use named ranges (e.g. *ServiceCreditsTotal*)
* Add data validation for percentage inputs

---

‚úî Cumulative Service Credit Chart

so tell me how does my personal office handles clients? their work, projects, programs, portfolios, contracts, accounts, offers, deals, fees, orders, payments, value ?

Here‚Äôs a **comprehensive operational framework** for how **your personal office** ‚Äî *The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm* ‚Äî should handle **clients, work, projects, programs, portfolios, contracts, accounts, offers, deals, fees, orders, payments, and value realization** across the Ashe/Pamoja ecosystem. This is built to match:

* **Your cooperative ecosystem**
* **Your Management Services Agreement (MSA) / service credits model**
* **Governance and compliance requirements**
* **Clear revenue & value capture flows**
* **Legal and tax defensibility**

I‚Äôll break it down into these sections:

1. **High-Level Client Engagement Model**
2. **Work & Project Intake / Delivery Lifecycle**
3. **Portfolio & Program Management**
4. **Contracts & Offers**
5. **Fees, Orders & Payment Terms**
6. **Recording Value, Credits & Compensation**
7. **Risk, Compliance & Governance**

This model works whether clients are coops within your ecosystem or, later, any outside organizations you serve.

---

# 1) üß≠ PERSONAL OFFICE ‚Äî CLIENT ENGAGEMENT MODEL

Your personal office is a **professional services provider** that delivers value via contractual relationships. It *does not* govern cooperatives or hold ownership rights unless explicitly agreed.

### Client Types

| Client Category                                                  | Typical Relationship      | Payment Profile           |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------- | ------------------------- |
| **Internal Coop Clients** (Ubuntuwa, federation coops, ventures) | MSA + Service Credits     | Deferred ‚Üí conversion     |
| **Program Clients** (Msingi programs)                            | MSA                       | Same accrual/credit model |
| **Hybrid / External** (future partners)                          | Standard MSA / consulting | Traditional fees          |
| **Personal Estate / Offices**                                    | Internal contracts        | Strategic billing         |

**Important:** Even internal engagements are treated as *services contracts* ‚Äî this prevents control confusion, tax ambiguity, and governance disputes.

---

# 2) üìå WORK & PROJECT MANAGEMENT LIFECYCLE

Your office should use a **consistent intake and delivery process**:

### A. Intake

1. **Client Request / Proposal**
   The client initiates a request ‚Äî documented with a Project Intake Form.
2. **Scope Definition**
   Aligns with Exhibit A (Scope of Work) in the MSA.
3. **Board / Governance Approval** *(if internal)*
   For cooperatives, the Board or authorized committee approves the engagement and any deferred compensation frameworks.

### B. Initiation

1. **Formal Contract Signing**
   MSA + SOW + Deferred Compensation Addendum (if applicable).
2. **Project Kickoff**
   Clarify deliverables, timelines, responsibilities, escalation paths.

### C. Execution

1. **Work Breakdown**
   Phase ‚Üí Deliverable ‚Üí Tasks ‚Üí Hours ‚Üí Assigned Dates.
2. **Weekly Work Logs**
   Track service hours (e.g., timesheets) tied to the Service Credit Ledger.

### D. Milestones

1. **Deliverable Acceptance**
   Clients review and give feedback.
2. **Integration & QA**
3. **Final Approval**

### E. Close

1. **Project Completion Report**
2. **Service Credit / Fee Reconciliation**

---

# 3) üß† PORTFOLIO & PROGRAM MANAGEMENT

As your clients grow, you‚Äôll have **multiple active workstreams**. Manage them as a **portfolio**:

### Portfolio Structure

| Active Projects         | Status   | Credits | Delivery Risk | Client Impact |
| ----------------------- | -------- | ------- | ------------- | ------------- |
| Governance OS Build     | OnTrack  | 120 hrs | Low           | High          |
| Integration Platform    | Planning | 80 hrs  | Medium        | High          |
| Program Curriculum Tech | Active   | 60 hrs  | Medium        | Medium        |

Use a **Portfolio Dashboard** showing:

* Project stage
* Hours provided
* Service credits accrued
* Estimated realization events

---

# 4) üìú CONTRACTS & OFFERS

### Contract Types

| Contract                                | Use Case                                   |
| --------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------ |
| **Management Services Agreement (MSA)** | Core long-term engagement                  |
| **Scope of Work (SOW)**                 | Defines deliverables for specific projects |
| **Deferred Compensation Addendum**      | Sweat equity compensation                  |
| **Statement of Work Change Order**      | Scope modifications                        |
| **External Consulting Agreement**       | Non-coop or outside entities               |

### Key Inclusions in All Contracts

* Scope of services
* Deliverables and acceptance criteria
* Compensation terms (cash, deferred credits)
* Term / termination clauses
* Confidentiality & IP rights
* Governing law & dispute resolution

*Your contracts should always be reviewed by counsel before execution.*

---

# 5) üí∞ FEES, ORDERS & PAYMENT TERMS

Since many of your clients will be internal coops or early-stage ventures, you need different **compensation modes** depending on revenue stage:

---

## A. Internal Coops / Deferred Compensation

**No upfront cash.** Instead, employ the lifecycle you already outlined:

### STAGE 1 ‚Äî Deferred Founder Services

* Services rendered, no invoicing or payable
* Tracked in **Service Credit Ledger**

### STAGE 2 ‚Äî Accrued Service Credits

* Once client has revenue, Board authorizes credit accrual
* Credits recorded *off-balance* (contingent)
* No immediate cash or income to you

### STAGE 3 ‚Äî Cash or Conversion

Choose one:

* **Cash Payment** ‚Äî you invoice, coop pays
* **Non-Voting Preferred Equity** ‚Äî Conversion Equity recorded
* **Patronage Allocation** ‚Äî If eligible, taxed as patronage income

**Tip:** Document each choice with a **Board Resolution**.

---

## B. External Clients / Traditional Fees

For external or commercial engagements (non-internal coops), use standard billing:

| Fee Type                              | Description                |
| ------------------------------------- | -------------------------- |
| **Hourly Retainer**                   | Billed monthly             |
| **Fixed Fee per Milestone**           | Predetermined deliverables |
| **Subscription / Monthly Management** | Ongoing services           |
| **Performance / Success Fee**         | Milestone-based bonus      |

Invoices should include:

* Work description
* Hours/rate
* Total amount
* Payment due terms (e.g., Net 30)

Late fees and collection policies must be specified.

---

# 6) üìä HOW VALUE IS RECOGNIZED & ACCOUNTED

Your firm must simultaneously manage:

* **Service Credit Ledger**
* **Accounts Receivable** (for cash engagements)
* **Deferred Compensation Records**
* **Revenue Recognition (when earned)**

### Internal Coops

| Stage        | Coop Records              | Your Office Records              |
| ------------ | ------------------------- | -------------------------------- |
| 1            | No GL entry               | No income                        |
| 2            | Contingent liability memo | Track service credits internally |
| 3A Cash      | Expense + cash reduction  | Revenue on receipt               |
| 3B Equity    | Equity issuance           | Income at FMV                    |
| 3C Patronage | Patronage allocation      | Income *per coop rules*          |

### External Clients

| Stage            | Coop/Client    | Your Office                  |
| ---------------- | -------------- | ---------------------------- |
| Contract signed  | No entry       | No entry                     |
| Work delivered   | Expense        | Revenue recognized (accrued) |
| Payment received | Cash reduction | Cash increase                |

---

# 7) üì¶ PAYMENT FLOW & VALUE REALIZATION

### Internal (Deferred)

1. You do the work.
2. Credits accrue.
3. Credits convert ‚Üí cash / equity / patronage.
4. Payment clears ‚Üí your office books revenue.

### External Clients

1. You deliver.
2. Invoice is issued.
3. Client pays.
4. Cash recognized, revenue booked.

**Value realization** for you happens at conversion or payment ‚Äî *not* when services are provided.

---

# 8) üîê LEGAL & TAX COMPLIANCE ‚Äî HOW TO HANDLE IT

### A. Legal Protections

* All engagements require written contracts.
* Include indemnity, limitation of liability, confidentiality.
* IP assignments/licensing should be explicit.

### B. Tax Responsibilities

Your office:

* Reports revenue on cash or FMV receipt
* Does not record income at Stage 1 or 2
* Records taxable events at Stage 3

Client/coops:

* Deduct fees when paid
* Follow coop patronage and tax reporting rules

### C. Governance Oversight

Any internal coop contract or credit conversion should be approved by:

* Board resolution
* Finance / audit committee
* Member notice (if material)

This protects you and the cooperative from challenges.

---

# 9) üß† CHECKLIST FOR EVERY CLIENT ENGAGEMENT

‚úî Signed MSA with approved SOW
‚úî Deferred Compensation Addendum for internal coops
‚úî Service Credit Ledger initiated
‚úî Clear milestone definitions
‚úî Board resolutions (where required)
‚úî Invoicing policies defined
‚úî Tax classification confirmed
‚úî Conflict of interest documented
‚úî Exit & termination provisions in place

---

# 10) üìå EXAMPLE FLOW ‚Äî INTERNAL COOP ENGAGEMENT

**Client:** Ubuntuwa Commons
**First 3 Months:**

* You deliver governance docs
* Service credits logged
* No cash yet

**Month 4:**

* Client generates revenue ‚Üí Board authorizes accrual
* Credits logged as contingent

**Month 8:**

* Client has sustainable revenue ‚Üí you convert credits to cash or equity
* Your office books income

**Month 9:**

* Payment received / equity issued ‚Üí tax event

---

# 11) üß† WHY THIS MODEL WORKS FOR YOU

‚úî Matches coop principles
‚úî Defers tax until payment or conversion
‚úî Separates governance from service delivery
‚úî Provides clarity in contracts
‚úî Keeps accounting defensible
‚úî Scales from internal clients to external ones

# ‚úÖ 3) BILLING & CASHFLOW FORECAST MODEL

*(Spreadsheet structure you can paste into Excel/Sheets)*

This model supports both **deferred service credits** and **cash billing**.

### **SHEET: INPUTS**

| Parameter          | Value                    |
| ------------------ | ------------------------ |
| Start Date         | [YYYY-MM-DD]             |
| End Date           | [YYYY-MM-DD]             |
| Hourly Rate        | [200]                    |
| Billing Model      | Deferred / Cash / Hybrid |
| Revenue Milestones | 250000                   |

---

### **SHEET: SERVICE LOG**

| Date       | Project  | Task        | Hours         | Rate | Service Credit ($) | Billable Cash ($) |
| ---------- | -------- | ----------- | ------------- | ---- | ------------------ | ----------------- |
| 2025-01-05 | Ubuntuwa | Arch Design | 10            | 200  | =C2*D2             | 0                 |
| 2025-01-12 | Ubuntuwa | Sprint Plan | 8             | 200  | =C3*D3             | 0                 |
| ‚Ä¶          | ‚Ä¶        | ‚Ä¶           | ‚Ä¶             | ‚Ä¶    | ‚Ä¶                  | ‚Ä¶                 |
| **Total**  |          |             | =SUM(C2:C100) |      | =SUM(F2:F100)      | =SUM(G2:G100)     |

---

### **SHEET: SERVICE CREDIT LEDGER**

| Period   | Credits Accrued | Revenue Milestone? | Notes                 |
| -------- | --------------- | ------------------ | --------------------- |
| Jan 2025 | 3800            | N                  | Pre-Revenue           |
| Feb 2025 | 4200            | N                  | ‚Ä¶                     |
| Mar 2025 | 5000            | Y                  | Revenue threshold hit |

---

### **SHEET: CASHFLOW FORECAST**

| Month     | Expected Cash Fees | Expected Equity Conversion Value | Net Cash Flow |
| --------- | ------------------ | -------------------------------- | ------------- |
| Jan       | 0                  | 0                                | 0             |
| Feb       | 0                  | 0                                | 0             |
| Mar       | 15000              | 0                                | 15000         |
| Apr       | 20000              | 5000                             | 25000         |
| ‚Ä¶         | ‚Ä¶                  | ‚Ä¶                                | ‚Ä¶             |
| **Total** | =SUM(B2:B100)      | =SUM(C2:C100)                    | =SUM(D2:D100) |

---

### üìä EXTRA FORMULAS

**Service Credit ($):**

```
=Hours * HourlyRate
```

**Net Cash Flow:**

```
=ExpectedCashFees + ExpectedEquityConversionValue
```

# ‚úÖ 4) BOARD RESOLUTION TEMPLATE

*For authorizing service credits and deferred compensation*

---

### **BOARD RESOLUTION OF [COOP NAME]**

**Date:** [YYYY-MM-DD]

**WHEREAS**, the Board of Directors of *[Coop]* recognizes that *The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm LLC* (‚ÄúProvider‚Äù) has been engaged under a Management Services Agreement to provide professional services in support of governance, systems, strategy, and delivery;

**WHEREAS**, the Board further acknowledges that Client has begun generating revenue and seeks to authorize the accrual of Service Credits for Provider in accordance with the Deferred Compensation Addendum attached to the Management Services Agreement;

**NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED THAT:**

1. The Board authorizes the accrual of Service Credits for services rendered by Provider through the Service Credit Ledger maintained by the Finance Team.

2. The Service Credit accrual rate is hereby established at $[Rate] per hour, as documented and approved.

3. The Service Credits shall be treated as contingent liabilities and shall not be recorded as expenses until realization per contractual terms.

4. Conversion of Service Credits to cash payment or other compensation (non-voting equity, patronage allocation, capital account) shall be permitted upon reaching defined revenue milestones as set forth in the Management Services Agreement and associated addenda.

5. The Board directs the Finance Officer to implement appropriate accounting procedures in accordance with audit and tax requirements.

**RESOLVED**, this  ____ day of _______***, 20***.

**BOARD OF DIRECTORS:**

---

[Name], Chair

---

[Name], Director

---

[Name], Director

‚úÖ How work gets scoped, delivered & tracked

# üìå OVERVIEW ‚Äî CLIENT LIFECYCLE STAGES

Your firm‚Äôs client lifecycle consists of **six major phases**:

1. **Discovery & Qualification**
2. **Proposal & Contracting**
3. **Engagement Planning & Kickoff**
4. **Delivery & Execution**
5. **Measurement, Billing & Credits**
6. **Closure & Ongoing Relationship**

Each phase has **specific actions, artifacts, and decisions** you must manage.

---

## üå± STAGE 1 ‚Äî DISCOVERY & QUALIFICATION

### **Purpose**

Determine whether the client is a good fit and what value you can deliver.

### **Activities**

üîπ Intake call or workshop
üîπ Clarify client needs
üîπ Align on strategic context (coop mission, revenue model)
üîπ Identify engagement type (deferred service / contractual fee)

### **Deliverables**

üìÑ Client Intake Form (filled)
üìå Qualified client list

### **Decision Criteria**

‚úî Are they a coop entity or external client?
‚úî Do they have revenue to pay?
‚úî Is Board approval needed (internal coop)?

---

## üìú STAGE 2 ‚Äî PROPOSAL & CONTRACTING

### **Purpose**

Define *what* services you‚Äôll deliver and *how* you‚Äôll get paid.

### **Activities**

üßæ Draft Scope of Work (SOW)
üìë Prepare Management Services Agreement (MSA)
üìÑ Prepare Deferred Compensation Addendum if needed
‚úî Get Board/Client signature

### **Artifacts**

* Signed MSA
* SOW
* Deferred Comp Addendum
* Board Resolution (if internal)

### **Checks**

‚úî Billing model (deferred vs cash)
‚úî Contribution tracking method
‚úî Client governance approval

---

## üó∫Ô∏è STAGE 3 ‚Äî ENGAGEMENT PLANNING & KICKOFF

### **Purpose**

Set expectations, timelines, teams, and tools.

### **Activities**

üîπ Hold kickoff meeting
üîπ Set delivery milestones
üîπ Establish communication cadence
üîπ Assign project roles (you, client reps)

### **Artifacts**

üìÖ Project Charter
üìß Kickoff Summary
üóÇ Setup tools (tracking, calendars, file repository)

### **Guidelines**

* Align delivery calendar with coop‚Äôs fiscal/calendar planning
* Clarify risk management and escalation paths

---

## ‚öôÔ∏è STAGE 4 ‚Äî DELIVERY & EXECUTION

### **Purpose**

Do the work efficiently, transparently, and systematically.

### **Activities**

üìå Work breakdown
üìå Task assignments
üìå Daily/weekly work logs
üìå Quality validation (QA checks)
üìå Client reviews

### **Artifacts**

üõ† Task Logs
üìÑ Deliverables (docs, biz models, code, designs)
üîÅ Change orders (if needed)

### **Tracking**

Use your **Service Credit Ledger** for internal/coop clients, or standard deliverable tracking for external clients.

---

## üßæ STAGE 5 ‚Äî MEASUREMENT, BILLING & SERVICE CREDITS

This is where **value meets money or credit**.

### **Internal Coop (Deferred Credits)**

* Record service hours ‚Üí service credits
* Track contingent liabilities
* Report to Board monthly/quarterly
* Maintain Service Credit Ledger

### **External Clients**

* Generate invoices
* Collect payments
* Record accounts receivable

### **Billing & Credits Artifacts**

üìä Monthly status + credit report
üßæ Invoices (external)
üìÖ Payment receipts / client sign-offs

### **Key Rules**

‚úî Convert credits only after revenue milestones
‚úî No taxable income until cash or property received
‚úî Board authorization required for credit accrual

---

## üü¶ STAGE 6 ‚Äî CLOSURE & ONGOING RELATIONSHIP

### **Purpose**

Wrap up the project formally and keep the client engaged.

### **Activities**

‚úî Deliver final acceptance docs
‚úî Conduct lessons learned review
‚úî Transfer knowledge / docs
‚úî Maintain relationship (follow-up)
‚úî Evaluate next phase opportunities

### **Artifacts**

üìÑ Project Completion Report
üìà Client Satisfaction Summary
üìû Follow-up plan

---

# üìå SAMPLE TIMELINES

| Phase                     | Duration             |
| ------------------------- | -------------------- |
| Intake & Contracting      | 1‚Äì2 weeks            |
| Kickoff & Planning        | 1‚Äì2 weeks            |
| Delivery (Sprints)        | 4‚Äì12 weeks per cycle |
| Billing / Credit Review   | Monthly / Quarterly  |
| Closure & Lessons Learned | 1‚Äì2 weeks            |

---

# üß† EXAMPLE SCENARIO (SIMULATED)

**Client:** Ubuntuwa Commons Coop
**Stage 1:**
‚úî Intake completed
‚úî MSA + Deferred Comp Addendum signed
‚úî Kickoff held

**Stage 2 ‚Äî Delivery:**
‚úî You log 100 hours in 8 weeks
‚úî Service Credit Ledger reflects $20K in credits
‚úî No bills issued

**Stage 3 ‚Äî Revenue:**
‚úî Coop hits $300K in revenue
‚úî Board authorizes Service Credit accrual

**Stage 4 ‚Äî Conversion:**
‚úî You elect cash conversion ‚Üí $20K payable
‚úî Invoice issued ‚Üí paid
‚úî Revenue booked in your office

---

# üìå WHY THIS WORKS FOR YOU

‚úî Protects you *from income recognition too early*
‚úî Keeps contracts and governance clean
‚úî Ensures services are traceable and billable
‚úî Aligns with cooperative principles
‚úî Makes switching to cash or equity conversion smooth

Here‚Äôs a **clear, practical guide** to handling **billing** for your personal office when:

‚úÖ Clients are early-stage cooperatives (or other clients)
‚úÖ They can‚Äôt pay you cash yet
‚úÖ You‚Äôre starting with **sweat equity and deferred compensation**
‚úÖ Payments won‚Äôt happen until they start generating revenue

This covers **how to structure billing terms, track work, communicate expectations, and get paid in a way that‚Äôs legally compliant, tax-defensible, and aligned with cooperative governance**.

---

# üìå FIRST: BILLING THINKING FOR PRE-REVENUE CLIENTS

Traditional invoicing doesn‚Äôt work if:

‚ùå There‚Äôs no revenue
‚ùå There‚Äôs no cash to pay
‚ùå You want to avoid early taxable income

So you need a **deferred billing model** tied to:

‚û° Your **Management Services Agreement (MSA)**
‚û° A **Service Credit Ledger**
‚û° Approved **milestones / revenue triggers**

This replaces ‚Äúbilling now‚Äù with **credits now, real money later**.

---

## üß† KEY PRINCIPLES

### 1) **Billing ‚â† Immediate Payment**

Work *results in credits*, not receivable invoices.
Credits are only monetized later.

### 2) **Credits are Contingent**

They are not real income until cash or property is received.

### 3) **Board Authorization Required (if internal coop)**

Your deferred billing terms must be approved by the coop‚Äôs board.

### 4) **Clear Documentation**

Every billable hour you work must be logged with:

* Project
* Date
* Hours
* Description of work
* Credit value

---

# üîπ BILLING MODEL ‚Äî STEP BY STEP

We‚Äôll walk through a **three-stage lifecycle** you already know:

## üß© STAGE 1 ‚Äî **No Billing Yet**

**Sweat Equity Starts**

Just **track work**:

üìã Use a *Service Credit Ledger*

* This is *not* an invoice
* It‚Äôs not a receivable
* It does *not* go onto the books as income or a receivable

Tools you should use:
‚úî Timesheet logs
‚úî Task tracking (Jira/Notion/Sheets)
‚úî Service Credit Ledger spreadsheet

At this stage:

```
No invoice issued
No accounts receivable
No income recognized
```

Just **track and report**.

---

## üß© STAGE 2 ‚Äî **Accrual of Credits**

Once the coop starts generating revenue OR the Board formally authorizes accrual:

üëâ You record **Service Credits** on the coop side as *off-balance contingent liabilities* (not normal receivables).

### What Your Billing Prep Looks Like

You generate a report that shows:

| Date  | Work Description | Hours | Rate | Credits Accrued |
| ----- | ---------------- | ----- | ---- | --------------- |
| Jan 3 | Governance Docs  | 10    | 200  | 2,000           |
| Jan 9 | Platform Design  | 8     | 200  | 1,600           |
| ‚Ä¶     | ‚Ä¶                | ‚Ä¶     | ‚Ä¶    | ‚Ä¶               |

Your credit report **is the basis for eventual billing**, but it‚Äôs not a formal invoice yet.

You can deliver this to the Board each period so they **authorize continuing accrual**.

---

## üß© STAGE 3 ‚Äî **Conversion to Cash / Equity / Patronage (Real Billing Event)**

This is where *actual billing happens*.

### You have three options

(we covered these on the unpaid/earned side already, but here‚Äôs how you record them)

---

### OPTION A ‚Äî **Cash Billing (Invoice)**

When the coop hits a revenue milestone and elects to pay cash:

**Invoice should include:**
‚úî Credit period covered
‚úî Service description
‚úî Hours & rate
‚úî Total amount due
‚úî Payment terms (e.g., Net 30)

Example (for $30,000 credits):

```
Invoice #XXX             Date: [date]
Bill To: Ubuntuwa Commons
Description           Hours  Rate   Amount
Governance Design      50   $200  $10,000
Platform Integration   40   $200   $8,000
Sprint Coordination    60   $200  $12,000
Total Due:                         $30,000
```

üìå Terms: Net 30
üìå Attach a copy of the Service Credit Ledger

**Accounting impact (client):**

```
DR Expense ‚Äì Professional Services  30,000
   CR Cash/Accounts Payable        30,000
```

**Your office recognizes revenue when cash is received:**

```
DR Cash                         30,000
   CR Service Revenue           30,000
```

---

### OPTION B ‚Äî **Conversion to Non-Voting Preferred Equity**

‚Ä¢ No invoice sent
‚Ä¢ No cash involved
‚Ä¢ You receive equity with FMV

**Board should pass a resolution** that:

‚úî Approves conversion of credits into equity
‚úî States FMV of equity issued

**Accounting (on coop books):**

```
DR Contingent Credits (liability)   XX
   CR Equity ‚Äì Non-Voting Preferred  XX
```

You record *income* when you receive the equity at FMV:

```
DR Equity (FMV)          XX
   CR Income ‚Äì Equity    XX
```

**Tax:** Your income equals FMV received (ordinary or separate category based on tax law).

---

### OPTION C ‚Äî **Patronage Allocation (if you are a member)**

‚Ä¢ Only if your office (or an entity you control) is a **member** of the coop
‚Ä¢ Credits convert to patronage allocations

Coop entries:

```
DR Contingent Credits             XX
   CR Patronage Allocation Payable XX
```

Your office upon receipt:

```
DR Patronage Allocation Receivable XX
   CR Patronage Income            XX
```

**Tax:** Taxable as patronage allocation (non-employee income).

---

# üìå BILLING BEST PRACTICES (EVERY CLIENT)

## 1. Always pair **Service Credits** with a formal **periodic report**

Do this monthly or quarterly:
‚úî Work completed
‚úî Hours logged
‚úî Credits accumulated
‚úî Mileage to next milestone (if any)

No Board approval ‚Üí no accrual.

---

## 2. Use a **consistent rate structure**

Either:
‚úî Hourly rate (e.g., $200/hr)
‚úî Task-based set values (e.g., governance doc = $5K)

Match rates to your SOW and MSA.

---

## 3. NEVER create traditional ‚Äúaccounts receivable‚Äù prematurely

Accounts receivable = **right to receive cash now**
You do *not* have that until conversion or cash billing event.

Instead, use:
üìå Contingent Credit / Off-Balance Ledger
üìå Internal Service Credit Tracking

---

## 4. Keep all correspondence

Always tie:
‚úî Work logs
‚úî Board resolutions
‚úî Periodic credit reports
‚úî SOW amendments
‚úî Invoices
‚úî Conversion elections

into one **engagement file**.

---

## 5. Align with governance

For internal coop clients:
‚úî Board must approve credit accrual
‚úî Board must approve conversion event
‚úî Your invoices / conversions should attach Board resolutions

---

# üìå TAX & AUDIT IMPLICATIONS

### **Deferred Billing Stage**

‚úî No income reported
‚úî No payroll taxes
‚úî No receivable recognized

DFS (Deferred Founder Services) = **non-taxed period**.

---

### **Accrual (Credits)**

‚úî Still no income
‚úî Contingent liability only

Audit will see:
‚úî Service Credit Ledger
‚úî Board resolutions authorizing accrual

---

### **Conversion / Cash Realization**

‚úî You report income when you **receive something of value**
‚úî Defer taxable event until that point

---

# üß† SAMPLE BILLING TIMELINE

| Week    | Activity                | Result                                               |
| ------- | ----------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| 1       | Kickoff + Intake        | No billing                                           |
| 1‚Äì4     | Deliver work, log hours | Service credits accrual starts                       |
| Month 2 | Board authorizes credit | Credits start accumulating official                  |
| Month 4 | Revenue milestone hit   | Credits continue + wait for conversion               |
| Month 6 | Client chooses cash     | Issue Invoice ‚Üí payment processed ‚Üí revenue recorded |

---

# üß† SAMPLE BILLING AFFORDABLE POLICY

**Payment Terms**

* Cash invoices: Net 30
* Equity conversions: Board resolution with FMV
* Patronage allocations: As allowed by bylaws

**Credit Validity**

* Service credits expire after 24 months if not realized

**Late Payment**

* If cash is due but not paid within 30 days: 2% monthly finance charge

---

# üìå ONE-PAGE BILLING GUIDELINES (FOR YOUR FILES)

**Billing Rule Summary**

1. No invoice until cash is possible
2. Track work as service credits
3. Use Board resolutions to authorize credits
4. Convert credits only at revenue milestones
5. Invoice only at cash realization event
6. Record income when value is received

üìï A **client billing policy document**
üìî A **template service credit report** for Board approval
üìä A **dashboard to show revenue vs credits vs cash flow**

Just tell me which one to generate next!

Absolutely ‚Äî here are **ready-to-use templates and models** you can drop into **Excel, Google Sheets, Word, or Google Docs** for:

üìà **Billing Automation Spreadsheet**
üìï **Client Billing Policy Document**
üìî **Template Service Credit Report (for Board Approval)**
üìä **Revenue vs. Credits vs. Cashflow Dashboard**

# üìà 1) BILLING AUTOMATION SPREADSHEET

*(Use this in Excel or Google Sheets)*

## **Sheet: Inputs**

| **Parameter**                    | **Cell** | **Value / Notes**        |
| -------------------------------- | -------- | ------------------------ |
| Start Date                       | B2       | yyyy-mm-dd               |
| End Date                         | B3       | yyyy-mm-dd               |
| Hourly Rate                      | B4       | e.g., 200                |
| Billing Model                    | B5       | Deferred / Cash / Hybrid |
| Revenue Milestone for Conversion | B6       | e.g., 250000             |
| Cash Tax Rate (%)                | B7       | e.g., 30%                |
| Equity Tax Rate (%)              | B8       | e.g., 30%                |
| Patronage Tax Rate (%)           | B9       | e.g., 25%                |

---

## **Sheet: Service Log**

| **Date**   | **Client** | **Project** | **Task**        |     **Hours** |   **Rate** |  **Credit $** |    **Cash $** |
| ---------- | ---------- | ----------- | --------------- | ------------: | ---------: | ------------: | ------------: |
| 2025-01-05 | Ubuntuwa   | Arch Design | Architecture    |            10 | =Inputs!B4 |        =E2*F2 |             0 |
| 2025-01-10 | Ubuntuwa   | Integration | API Integration |             8 | =Inputs!B4 |        =E3*F3 |             0 |
| ‚Ä¶          | ‚Ä¶          | ‚Ä¶           | ‚Ä¶               |             ‚Ä¶ |          ‚Ä¶ |             ‚Ä¶ |             ‚Ä¶ |
| **Totals** |            |             |                 | =SUM(E2:E100) |            | =SUM(G2:G100) | =SUM(H2:H100) |

---

## **Sheet: Service Credit Ledger**

| **Period**        | **Credits Accrued** | **Revenues** | **Revenue ‚â• Milestone?**   | **Board OK? (Y/N)** |
| ----------------- | ------------------- | ------------ | -------------------------- | ------------------- |
| Jan 2025          | =ServiceLog!G2:G31  | 120000       | =IF(C2>=Inputs!B6,"Y","N") |                     |
| Feb 2025          | =ServiceLog!G32:G61 | 90000        | =IF(C3>=Inputs!B6,"Y","N") |                     |
| ‚Ä¶                 | ‚Ä¶                   | ‚Ä¶            | ‚Ä¶                          |                     |
| **Total Credits** | =SUM(B2:B100)       |              |                            |                     |

---

## **Sheet: Conversion & Billing**

### **Cash Conversion**

| Description   | Formula                   | Result     |
| ------------- | ------------------------- | ---------- |
| Total Credits | =ServiceCreditLedger!B101 | $XX        |
| Choose Cash % | Manual Input              | e.g., 100% |
| Cash Portion  | =B2*CashPct               |            |
| Cash Tax      | =CashPortion*Inputs!B7    |            |
| Net Cash      | =CashPortion-CashTax      |            |

### **Equity Conversion**

| Description          | Formula                   | Result   |
| -------------------- | ------------------------- | -------- |
| Total Credits        | =ServiceCreditLedger!B101 |          |
| Equity %             | Manual                    | e.g., 0% |
| Equity Portion       | =B2*EquityPct             |          |
| FMV (Board-approved) | Manual Input              |          |
| Equity Tax           | =FMV*Inputs!B8            |          |
| Net Equity           | =FMV-EquityTax            |          |

### **Patronage Conversion**

| Description     | Formula                      | Result |
| --------------- | ---------------------------- | ------ |
| Total Credits   | =ServiceCreditLedger!B101    |        |
| Patronage %     | Manual                       |        |
| Patronage Value | =B2*PatronagePct             |        |
| Patronage Tax   | =PatronageValue*Inputs!B9    |        |
| Net Patronage   | =PatronageValue-PatronageTax |        |

---

# üìä 2) REVENUE VS CREDITS VS CASHFLOW DASHBOARD

*(Use charts in Sheets or Excel)*

### **Suggested Chart Elements**

   * X-axis: Period (Month)
   * Y-axis: Cumulative Credits (Service Credit Ledger)

   * X-axis: Revenues by month
   * Y-axis: Credits accrued

   * Line chart:

     * Cash Inflow (predicted)
     * Cash Outflow (expected fees)
     * Net Flow

# üìï 3) CLIENT BILLING POLICY DOCUMENT

*(Word / Google Docs template)*

---

### **CLIENT BILLING POLICY ‚Äî The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm**

**Effective Date:** [YYYY-MM-DD]
**Version:** 1.0

---

## 1. **Purpose**

This policy explains how the Firm records, tracks, and realizes compensation for services delivered to clients ‚Äî including deferred billing, service credits, and revenue recognition.

---

## 2. **Scope**

Applies to all client engagements, including:

* Deferred compensation arrangements with cooperative clients
* Standard fee engagements
* Hybrid billing models

---

## 3. **Definitions**

**Service Credits:** Value assigned to work delivered when cash payment is deferred.
**Realization Event:** An occurrence (typically revenue milestone) that permits Service Credits to convert to cash or equity.
**Billing Event:** A recognized point at which the Firm issues an invoice or receives value.

---

## 4. **Billing Principles**

1. **No Cash Billing Until Client Has Revenue.**
   Service Credits are tracked, not invoiced, until a realization event has occurred.

2. **Service Credits Must Be Board-Authorized (Internal Coops).**
   Prior to accrual, the client Board must approve credit terms and tracking.

3. **Invoices May Be Issued Only After Conversion Election.**
   Cash billing events happen post-realization (Net 30 terms unless otherwise stated).

4. **Deferred Compensation Is Not Recognized as Income Until Realized.**
   This aligns with GAAP and tax treatment of contingent compensation.

---

## 5. **Service Credit Tracking**

* A Service Credit Ledger will be maintained for each client.
* Credits are logged with date, description, hours, and rate.
* Monthly summaries will be provided to the client governance body.

---

## 6. **Conversion Events**

At or after a revenue milestone, credit holders may elect:

* Cash payment
* Non-voting equity conversion
* Patronage allocation

Conversion elections shall be documented in writing and approved by client governance where required.

---

## 7. **Invoicing Terms (Cash Fee Clients)**

* Invoices are issued monthly or upon milestone completion.
* Standard payment is *Net 30*.
* Late fees of 2% per month may be applied on overdue balances.

---

## 8. **Tax Treatment**

The Firm recognizes income only upon **receipt of cash or property**, in accordance with applicable tax laws.

---

## 9. **Revisions**

This policy will be reviewed annually or as needed.

# üìÑ MANAGEMENT SERVICES AGREEMENT

**(The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm ‚Äì Client Engagement Contract)**

**This Management Services Agreement** (‚ÄúAgreement‚Äù) is entered into as of **[Effective Date]**, by and between:

**Provider:**
**The Dominic Eaton Software Engineering Firm LLC**
(‚ÄúProvider‚Äù)
Principal Office: [Provider Address]
Business Entity ID: [LLC/State Filing #]

and

**Client:**
**[Client Legal Name]**
(‚ÄúClient‚Äù)
Principal Office: [Client Address]

Collectively, the Provider and Client may be referred to herein as the ‚ÄúParties‚Äù or individually as a ‚ÄúParty.‚Äù

---

## **1. ENGAGEMENT & SERVICES**

**1.1 Engagement.**
Client hereby engages Provider to perform certain professional services as described in **Exhibit A** (Scope of Work), and Provider agrees to perform such services pursuant to the terms of this Agreement.

**1.2 Standard of Performance.**
Provider shall perform services in a professional, workmanlike manner consistent with industry standards.

**1.3 Subcontractors.**
Provider may use subcontractors but remains responsible for performance.

---

## **2. TERM & TERMINATION**

**2.1 Term.**
This Agreement begins on the Effective Date and continues until **[Termination Date or ‚Äúcompletion of services‚Äù]** unless earlier terminated under this Section.

**2.2 Termination for Convenience.**
Either Party may terminate this Agreement upon **30 days‚Äô written notice**.

**2.3 Termination for Cause.**
Either Party may terminate immediately if the other materially breaches and fails to cure within **15 days** after written notice.

**2.4 Effect of Termination.**
Sections concerning compensation, intellectual property, confidentiality, tax, and indemnity shall survive termination.

---

## **3. COMPENSATION & PAYMENT TERMS**

**3.1 Compensation Models.**
Provider may be compensated in one or more of the following ways (as defined in Exhibit B):

A) **Deferred Founder Services (Stage 1)** ‚Äî no cash payment now; service work tracked for future realization.
B) **Accrued Service Credits (Stage 2)** ‚Äî service work accrues credits tied to milestones.
C) **Conversion/Payment Events (Stage 3)** ‚Äî credits may be converted to cash, non-voting equity, patronage allocations, or capital account credits.

**3.2 Deferred Compensation.**
Provider acknowledges that deferred compensation does *not* create a present enforceable right until realization criteria are met.

**3.3 Invoicing & Payments.**
When cash payment applies, Provider shall issue invoices per timelines in Exhibit B. Client shall pay invoices within **Net 30** days.

**3.4 Expenses.**
Client shall reimburse pre-approved, reasonable out-of-pocket expenses.

---

## **4. SERVICE CREDITS, MILESTONES & CONVERSION**

**4.1 Service Credit Ledger.**
All deferred work is tracked in a Service Credit Ledger, maintained by Provider and reviewed by Client governance per Exhibit B.

**4.2 Revenue Milestones.**
Conversion of credits is contingent on revenue milestones defined in Exhibit B or otherwise approved by Client‚Äôs governance body.

**4.3 Conversion Options.**
Provider may elect at or after realization events to receive compensation by:

A) Cash payment
B) Non-voting preferred equity
C) Patronage allocations (if Client membership applies)
D) Capital account credits

**4.4 Board Authorization.**
For clients operating as cooperatives, Service Credit accruals and conversions require formal approval by Client‚Äôs Board or authorized governance body.

---

## **5. REPORTING & ACCEPTANCE**

**5.1 Status Reports.**
Provider shall provide regular status reports showing work completed, credits accrued, and progress toward milestones.

**5.2 Deliverable Acceptance.**
Deliverables shall be subject to Client review and acceptance procedures described in Exhibit A.

---

## **6. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY**

**6.1 Ownership.**
Deliverables created expressly under this Agreement shall be owned by Client, subject to licensing terms.

**6.2 License Back.**
Client grants Provider a non-exclusive license to use such deliverables for internal business and portfolio documentation.

---

## **7. CONFIDENTIALITY**

**7.1 Confidential Information.**
Each Party agrees to protect Confidential Information of the other and use it only to perform obligations under this Agreement.

**7.2 Exceptions.**
Confidentiality obligations do not apply to publicly known information, independently developed info, or disclosures required by law.

---

## **8. INDEPENDENT CONTRACTOR**

**8.1 Relationship.**
Provider is an independent contractor; nothing shall create an employer-employee, partnership, or joint venture relationship.

**8.2 Tax Treatment.**
Provider is responsible for its own tax reporting and obligations.

---

## **9. REPRESENTATIONS & WARRANTIES**

**9.1 Mutual Warranty.**
Each Party represents that it has the power and authority to enter this Agreement.

**9.2 Provider Warranty.**
Provider warrants services shall be performed with professional skill and care.

---

## **10. LIMITATION OF LIABILITY**

Neither Party shall be liable for indirect, incidental, special, or consequential damages.

Maximum liability shall not exceed the aggregate fees paid to Provider under this Agreement.

---

## **11. INDEMNITY**

Each Party shall indemnify and hold harmless the other from third-party claims arising out of breach of representations, negligence, or willful misconduct.

---

## **12. GENERAL PROVISIONS**

**12.1 Governing Law.**
This Agreement shall be governed by the laws of *[State/Country]*.

**12.2 Entire Agreement.**
This Agreement and its Exhibits constitute the entire understanding.

**12.3 Amendment.**
No amendment is effective unless in writing and signed by both Parties.

## üìå FIELDS EXPLAINED

### **Group**

High-level classification such as governance, operating ventures, programs, or personal/estate.

### **Client (Entity)**

The legal/organizational name.

### **Brief Description / Profile**

What the client *is* and *why they engage your firm*.

### **Portfolio Area**

Broad area of work (e.g., governance tech, OS integration, research).

### **Contract Type**

Base contract used:

* **MSA:** Management Services Agreement
* **MSA + Deferred Comp Addendum:** For early revenue coop clients
* **LPA Support:** For hybrid capital vehicles such as Mande Investment Group
* **N/A:** For internal personal office operations

### **Deliverables / Services**

Typical service categories you provide:

* Systems architecture
* Governance frameworks
* Platform engineering
* Integration tooling
* Program design
* Capital tech

### **Status / Notes**

High-level status, such as strategic client, operational client, or program stage.

Absolutely ‚Äî below is a **comprehensive, continuous Work Breakdown Structure (WBS)** for your firm‚Äôs **Year 1 plan** to get *all of your firm‚Äôs clients* up, running, and live. It‚Äôs **grouped by WBS ‚Üí Packages ‚Üí Themes ‚Üí Initiatives ‚Üí Epics ‚Üí Stories**, and includes:

‚úÖ IDs (W, P, TH, I, E, S)
‚úÖ Name, Type, Brief, Start, Duration
‚úÖ Assigned Member / Team
‚úÖ Logical structuring by your delivery and ecosystem needs

### How this table is organized

*Each row is hierarchical and comes with:*

* **ID** ‚Äî Unique ID for WBS / package / theme / initiative / epic / story
* **Name** ‚Äî Clear, actionable name
* **Type** ‚Äî (strategy, plan, tactic, milestone, epic, story type, etc.)
* **Brief** ‚Äî Short description of purpose
* **Start** ‚Äî Start date
* **Dur** ‚Äî Duration in business days (d) or sprints/quarters
* **Owner** ‚Äî Member / Team responsible

### Teams & Members

Assigned team types reflect your future org model:

**Teams**

* **Squad** ‚Äî delivery teams
* **Chapter** ‚Äî domain expertise group
* **Tribe** ‚Äî cross-team alignment
* **Tiger** ‚Äî rapid response task group
* **Guild** ‚Äî community of practice
* **Domain** ‚Äî business domain owner
* **Line** ‚Äî horizontal service line

### üß† NOTES

**1. Start Dates & Durations**
‚Ä¢ Dates are sequenced logically, allowing dependencies (e.g., you can only convert credits after milestones).
‚Ä¢ Durations assume a working year of ~260 business days.

**2. Assigned Owners**
‚Ä¢ Members/Teams reflect your firm‚Äôs structure and people you‚Äôll recruit early.

**3. Story Types**
‚Ä¢ Stories capture different delivery units (feature, test, requirement, documentation).

**4. Time Structures**
‚Ä¢ You can map these tasks to **Sprints (2 weeks)**, **PI** (quarter cycles), **Timeboxes**.

**5. Integration & Quality**
‚Ä¢ QA and Governance tests are sequenced after features.

Great question ‚Äî **legal and legal entity management** is critical for your firm and ecosystem, and it *should be owned by someone with the right skill set*. Let‚Äôs break this down clearly and practically.

---

# üß† 1. **Current 8-Person Core Team: Legal Coverage**

Here are your **existing core roles** and how they relate to legal work:

| Role                              | Legal / Entity Responsibilities                                      | Covered?                       |
| --------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------ |
| **Dominic (CEO/Founder)**         | Strategic legal risk, entity formation decisions, executive sign-off | ‚úî (lead)                       |
| **Chief of Staff**                | Process compliance, ensuring tasks get executed                      | ‚ö† (oversight only)             |
| **Program Sequencer**             | Phase gate compliance sequencing                                     | ‚ö† (alignment only)             |
| **OVCS Liaison / Governance Sec** | Governance documentation, OVCS submissions                           | ‚úî (partial ‚Äî governance legal) |
| **Ops & Admin Lead**              | Administrative contracts, invoicing tools, vendors                   | ‚ö† (execution support)          |
| **Financial Controller**          | Financial compliance (tax/expense)                                   | ‚ö† (interface with legal)       |
| **Technical Architect**           | Tech standards risk, IP boundaries                                   | ‚ö† (tech risk)                  |
| **Communications Lead**           | Messaging/legal coordination                                         | ‚ö† (coordination)               |
| **Executive Assistant**           | Scheduling & coordination                                            | ‚úñ                              |

**Key insight:**
Your team *already covers governance, documentation, and administrative contract workflows*, but **no one currently owns core legal functions** such as:

* Legal entity formation & maintenance
* Regulatory compliance (corporate / cooperative / tax)
* Intellectual property rights management
* Contract drafting & review beyond templates
* Risk & liability mitigation
* Jurisdictional entity management

The closest role with partial exposure is the **OVCS Liaison / Governance Secretary**, but that role is **governance-focused**, not full legal coverage.

---

# üß† 2. **Do You Need a Dedicated Core Legal Role?**

**Yes ‚Äî you need a dedicated legal ownership role.**

Without this, you risk:

‚úî Incorrect entity formation
‚úî Non-compliant contracts
‚úî Undocumented liabilities
‚úî Tax/legal mismatches across jurisdictions
‚úî Governance disputes
‚úî Weak intellectual property protection

Especially since your ecosystem is a *composite of coops, federated entities, and hybrid structures*, you must build a **Legal & Entity Management function** with clear ownership.

---

# üß† 3. **Where Legal Entity Management Fits in the Org**

You have 3 options for how to cover this:

### **A) Add a Full-Time ‚ÄúLegal & Entity Steward‚Äù to the Core Team**

This would become **hire #9** in your strategic staffing plan.

**Responsibilities**

* Entity charters & maintenance (coops/federation entities)
* Compliance with state/federal requirements
* Corporate records, minutes, filings, renewals
* Contract review & risk management
* IP protection & licensing
* Regulatory strategy for hybrid capital operations

**Ideal Profile**

* JD or equivalent legal qualifications
* Experience with cooperatives / nontraditional entity forms
* Multi-jurisdiction experience
* Contract negotiation + compliance experience

---

### **B) Scale Legal via External Counsel + Internal Steward**

If full-time isn‚Äôt justified yet, pair:

**Internal Steward (part-time hire or consultant)**

* **External Legal Counsel (specialized law firm)**

**Internal Legal Steward Responsibilities**

* Manage entity documents
* Coordinate filings & renewals
* Align contracts with legal counsel
* Pre-screen legal risk

This is more cost-efficient early on.

---

### **C) Expand OVCS Liaison Into ‚ÄúLegal & Entity Steward‚Äù**

You could evolve the **OVCS Liaison / Governance Secretary** role to include entity compliance.

However, this person must be:

* Legally trained or deeply familiar with entity law
* Responsible for:

  * Corporate governance documentation
  * Legal entity lifecycle (formation ‚Üí compliance ‚Üí dissolution)
  * Contract risk and review workflows

This *expands beyond governance messaging into legal authority* and should be explicitly defined.

---

# üß† 4. **Recommended Placement**

Your **ideal legal ownership structure** for Year 1:

```
                             +----------------------+
                             | Dominic (CEO/Founder)|
                             +----------+-----------+
                                        |
                 +----------------------+---------------------+
                 |                      |                     |
         +-------+------+       +-------+------+     +--------+--------+
         | CoS (Ops Integrator)|  Legal & Entity Steward| FinCtrl |
         +---------------------+                       +----------------+
```

**Why this works:**

* Dominic remains strategic lead
* CoS coordinates execution
* **Legal & Entity Steward** owns all legal risk
* Financial Controller coordinates tax/legal compliance
* Ops Lead supports filings and admin

---

# üß† 5. **Draft Role Description ‚Äî Legal & Entity Steward**

Use this as a **template job/profile**:

### **Title:** Legal & Entity Steward

**Alias:** Legal Steward, Entity Legal Manager

**Reports To:** Chief of Staff / CEO

**Primary Function:**
Owns legal entity governance, compliance, contracts, risk mitigation, and entity maintenance across the Ashe / Pamoja ecosystem.

**Core Responsibilities**

* Manage entity formation and maintenance

  * Registrations
  * Renewals
  * Jurisdiction compliance
* Draft/review contracts and legal instruments

  * MSAs
  * Services agreements
  * Bylaws & governance docs
  * Conversion terms
* Legal risk assessment and consultation
* Intellectual Property strategy & protection
* Support tax compliance reporting
* Interface with external counsel
* Build legal entity management playbooks

**Authority**

* Final approval on legal templates and contracts
* Gatekeeper for entity compliance
* Escalation authority for legal risk

**Ideal Profile**

* Licensed attorney or equivalent
* Cooperative & multi-entity legal experience
* Contract & compliance expertise
* Cross-jurisdiction knowledge
